Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from Sharh al-Hidayah (Ashraf al-Hadaya) discusses the methods of appointing a qasim (partition judge) by the qadi. It explains that the qadi has two options: first, to appoint a qasim whose salary is paid from the public treasury (bayt al-mal) because his benefit is general to all Muslims; second, if he does not do that, he can appoint a qasim who takes a fee from the partners seeking division, since the benefit here is specific to them. The preferred method is the first, as it avoids any suspicion of bias. The author adds a note warning against corruption in later times, emphasizing that the task of appointing qasims should be handled by the ruler to prevent bribery.

Key Terms
قاسم (qasim): A person appointed by the qadi to divide property among co-owners according to sharia.
بیت المال (bayt al-mal): The public treasury of the Muslim state; funds for public expenses.
اجر مثل (ajr mithl): The standard or equivalent fee for similar work, used to prevent exploitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The partners pay his fee directly.
B) He receives a salary from the public treasury (bayt al-mal).
C) He works for free.
D) The qadi pays him from his own pocket.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits two compensation methods for a qasim, but the salary from bayt al-mal is preferred to avoid suspicion and serve the public good.

Conditions Required in a Qasim: Justice, Trustworthiness, Knowledge
States the three obligatory qualities for a qasim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three obligatory conditions for a qasim in Hanafi law and explain the rationale behind each condition.

Core Idea
A qasim must be just, trustworthy, and knowledgeable—these are wajib conditions because he performs judicial work.

This passage from Al-Hidayah outlines the essential qualities a qasim (arbitrator or divider of shares) must possess. The author explains that since the qasim acts in a capacity similar to a qadi, he must meet the same fundamental criteria: 'adl (justice), amanah (trustworthiness), and 'ilm bi al-qisma (knowledge of partition). Understanding these conditions is critical for anyone involved in Islamic judicial procedure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
Locate the three qualities the passage explicitly requires for a qasim: justice ('adl), trustworthiness (amana), and knowledge of division ('ilm bi al-qisma).
2
Determine the legal ruling
The passage uses the word 'wajib' (obligatory) for these conditions. Confirm that the ruling level is wajib, not just recommended.
3
Understand the rationale
The passage gives two reasons: (1) the qasim's work is a type of qada (judicial function), so the same qualities as a qadi are needed; (2) effective division requires capability (qudra), which depends on knowledge, and reliability (i'timad), which depends on trustworthiness.
Capability requires knowledge; reliability requires trustworthiness.
4
Apply to a hypothetical
Consider a scenario where a qasim is appointed who is just and trustworthy but lacks knowledge of division. According to this passage, that appointment would be invalid because the wajib condition of knowledge is missing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی قاسم عادل، مامون قسمت کو جاننے والا مقرر کرے ويجب ان يكون عدلا مامونا عالما بالقسمة لانه من جنس عمل القضاء ولانه لابد من القدرة وهى بالعلم ومن الاعتماد على قوله وهو بالامانة ترجمہ اور واجب ہے کہ قاسم عادل ہو مامون ہو قسمت کو جاننے والا ہو اسلئے کہ یہ قضاء کے عمل کی جنس سے ہے اور اسلئے کہ قدرت کا ہونا ضروری ہے اور قدرت علم کے ذریعہ ہوگی اور اس کے قول پر اعتمادضروری ہے اور یہ امانت کے ذریعہ ہوگا۔ تشریح قاضی کے اندر ان تین اوصاف کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ سعا دل ہو، امانت دار ہو اور تقسیم کے مسائل سے واقف ہو کیونکہ تقسیم بھی ایک قسم کی قضاء ہے تو قاضی کے اوصاف اسکے اندر ہونے چاہئیں اور تقسیم کیلئے اس پر قدرت ضروری ہے اور قدرت علم سے ہوگی نیز اس کے قول پر اعتماد ضروری ہے اور اعتماد جب ہوگا جبکہ وہ عادل اور امانت دار ہو۔
The qadi appoints a qasim who is just, trustworthy, and knowledgeable about division. And it is obligatory that he be just, trustworthy, and knowledgeable about division because it is a type of judicial work, and because capability is necessary, and capability is through knowledge, and reliance on his statement is necessary, and that is through trustworthiness. Translation: And it is obligatory that the qasim be just, trustworthy, and knowledgeable about division because this is of the same genus as the work of qada, and because capability is necessary, and capability is through knowledge, and reliance on his statement is necessary, and that is through trustworthiness. Explanation: It is necessary for the qadi to possess these three qualities. He should be a just person, trustworthy, and acquainted with the issues of division. Because division is also a type of qada, so the qualities of a qadi should be present in him. And for division, capability is necessary, and capability is through knowledge. Also, reliance on his statement is necessary, and reliance occurs when he is just and trustworthy.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage establishes the obligatory (wajib) conditions for a qasim. Because the qasim performs a judicial function (qada), he must meet the same fundamental criteria as a qadi: he must be 'adil (just), ma'min (trustworthy), and 'alim bi al-qisma (knowledgeable in the law of partition). The reasoning is that competence (qudra) requires knowledge, and credibility (i'timad) requires trustworthiness. The Urdu commentary emphasizes that these three qualities are necessary for the qasim just as they are for the qadi.

Key Terms
عدل (adl): In this context, the quality of being upright and avoiding major sins and persistence on minor sins.
امانة (amana): Trustworthiness; that the qasim is reliable and not suspected of dishonesty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Qadi Must Not Compel People to Use a Single Qasim
Prohibition on forcing parties to hire a specific qasim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a qadi may not force parties to hire a specific qasim and explain the legal reasoning based on the prohibition of compulsion in contracts (jabr 'ala al-aqd).

Core Idea
Contracts require free consent; the qadi cannot compel anyone to hire a specific partitioner.

This lesson addresses a specific ruling from Hanafi fiqh concerning the role of the qadi in property partition disputes. The passage prohibits the judge from forcing the parties to use a particular qasim (partition arbitrator). The underlying principle is that hiring a qasim is a contract (ijara), and compulsion in contracts is invalid. Additionally, a monopoly could lead to exploitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Prohibited Act
What exactly is prohibited? The qadi compelling people to use a single qasim (a partitioner) for their property division.
2
Understand the Legal Principle
Recognize that the hiring of a qasim is a rental contract (ijara). Islamic law prohibits compulsion in contracts (la jabr 'ala al-uqud).
The Arabic term used is 'jabr 'ala al-aqd'.
3
Recognize the Secondary Reason
If the qadi designates only one qasim, that qasim may exploit his monopoly and charge excessive fees.
This is a consequence of compulsion, not a separate ruling.
4
Apply the Ruling
What should the qadi do instead? He should leave the parties free to choose any qualified qasim, or offer a list but not force a single choice.
The ruling protects contractual freedom and prevents exploitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی ایک ہی قاسم پر لوگوں کو مجبور نہ کرے ولا يجبر القاضى الناس على قاسم واحد معناه لا يجبرهم على ان يستاجره ولانه لا جبر على العقود ولانه لو تعين لتحكم بالزيادة على اجر مثله ترجمہ اور قاضی لوگوں کو ایک قاسم پر مجبور نہ کرے اسکے معنی ہیں کہ ان کو مجبور نہ کرے اس بات پر کہ وہ اسی کو امیر مقرر کریں اسلئے کہ عقود پر جبر نہیں ہوتا اور اسلئے کہ اگر وہی متعین ہو گیا تو وہ حکام کرے گا زیادتی کے ساتھ اپنے مثل کی اجرت پر ۔ تشریح یعنی قاضی لوگوں کو مجبور نہ کرے کہ اسی قاسم سے بٹوارہ کرائیں کیونکہ یہ جبر علی العقد ہے حالانکہ عقود میں جبر نہیں چلتا۔ اور اگر قاضی ایک ہی کو متعین کرے گا تو وہ اوگوں سے زیادہ اجرت لے گا یہ سمجھتے ہوئے کہ میرے علاوہ تو اور قاسم ہے نہیں ۔
The qadi should not force people to use a single qasim. And he should not force people to use a single qasim. Its meaning: he should not force them to hire him, because there is no compulsion in contracts, and because if he is exclusively appointed, he will act arbitrarily by charging more than the equivalent fee. Translation: And the qadi should not force people to use a single qasim. Its meaning: he should not force them to make him (the specific qasim) their appointed one, because there is no compulsion in contracts, and because if he becomes exclusive, he will act arbitrarily by charging more than the equivalent fee. Explanation: That is, the qadi should not force people to get their partition done only by that qasim, because this is compulsion in a contract (jabr 'ala al-aqd), while contracts are not subject to compulsion. And if the qadi designates only one, he will take more fee from people, thinking that there is no other qasim besides him.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage forbids the qadi from compelling the parties to a partition to use only one specific qasim. The reasons given are: (1) contracts (such as the hiring of a qasim) cannot be coerced; (2) if only one qasim is available, he might exploit his monopoly by charging excessive fees. The Urdu commentary clarifies that this prohibition applies because it constitutes 'jabr 'ala al-aqd' — compulsion in a contract — which is invalid in Islamic law.

Key Terms
جبر على العقد (jabr 'ala al-aqd): Compulsion in entering a contract, which is prohibited in Islamic law.

C) Because the qadi has no authority over qasims.
D) Because it leads to higher fees for the qadi.

Key Takeaway
The qadi must not compel the use of a single partitioner because contracts require free consent and monopoly leads to exploitation.

Voluntary Division of Property by Co-Owners
Ruling on partners dividing property without a qasim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on partners dividing property voluntarily and identify when the qadi's intervention is required.

Core Idea
Adult co-owners may divide property by mutual agreement; a minor without a guardian requires qadi's permission.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies the permissibility of co-owners partitioning shared property without official appointment. It draws a critical distinction: when all parties are legally competent adults, mutual consent suffices. However, if a minor is among them and lacks a guardian, the partners cannot act for him — only the qadi, as general guardian, can authorize the division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is the voluntary division of shared property by the co-owners themselves. The default ruling: permissible (mubah) when all co-owners are adults.
2
Identify the exception
The text introduces an exception with 'illa' (except): when a minor (saghir) is among the co-owners.
The exception is only triggered if the minor has no guardian.
3
Understand the reason for the exception
The reason is lack of wilaya (legal authority). Adult co-owners have no authority over the minor's share; only the qadi (or the minor's own guardian) can act.
Qadi has general guardianship (wilaya 'amma) over minors without specific guardians.
4
Apply the condition of whether a guardian exists
If the minor has a guardian (father, grandfather, or executor), that guardian can act on his behalf without needing the qadi. If not, the qadi must intervene.
The commentary mentions 'if the child has a representative (na'ib), then the need for the qadi's judgment does not arise.'
5
State the practical consequence (thamarah)
Without a guardian, the partition is invalid without qadi's order; with a guardian, it is valid by mutual agreement.
The mufta bihi position is that partners may divide by themselves; minor requires qadi unless represented.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اصطلحوا فاقتموا جاز الا اذا كان فيهم صغير فيحتاج الى امر القاضى لانه لا ولاية لهم عليه ترجمہ اور اگر شر کا اتفاق کرلیں پس آپس میں ہزارہ کر لیں تو جائز ہے مگر جبکہ ان میں کوئی بچہ ہوتو قاضی کے فیصلہ کی جانب حاجت پیش آوے گی اسلئے کہ ان کو ولایت نہیں ہے۔ تشریح اگر شرکاء خود اتفاق سے تقسیم کر لیں تو جائز ہے لیکن اگر ان میں کوئی بچہ ہو اور اس کا باپ یا وصی نہ ہو تو پھر قاضی کے فیصلہ کی حاجت پیش آئے گی کیونکہ شرکاء کو بچہ پر ولایت نہیں ہے اور قاضی کی ولایت عام ہے۔ اگر بچہ کا نائب ہو تو پھر قضاء قاضی کی حاجت پیش نہیں آئے گی ۔
And if they settle amicably and then divide among themselves, it is permissible, except when there is a minor among them, then they need the order of the qadi because they have no authority over him. Translation: And if the partners agree among themselves and then divide (the property), it is permissible, except when there is a child among them, then they will need the decision of the qadi because they have no guardianship over him. Explanation: If the partners themselves agree and divide, it is permissible. But if there is a minor among them and he has no father or guardian, then the judgment of the qadi will be needed because the partners have no guardianship over the child, and the qadi has general guardianship. If the child has a representative, then the need for the qadi's judgment does not arise.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage states that co-owners may partition their shared property by mutual agreement without requiring a qadi-appointed qasim. However, if one of the co-owners is a minor (saghir) who has no father or guardian present, then the qadi must intervene because the adults have no legal authority (wilaya) over the minor. The qadi, as the general guardian (wali 'am), can authorize the partition. If the minor has a guardian (father or executor), then the guardian can act on his behalf without needing the qadi.

Key Terms
ولایت (wilaya): Legal authority to act on behalf of another, especially over minors.
صغیر (saghir): A minor child who has not reached puberty and is not legally independent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Qadi’s Duty to Prevent Price-Fixing Among Qasims
Ruling on qadi forbidding qasims from colluding to raise fees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a qadi must forbid qasims from colluding to fix fees, and explain the rationale based on preventing harm to the public.

Core Idea
A qadi must prevent qasims from colluding to keep fees affordable through competition.

This ruling addresses a public policy concern: court-appointed property dividers (qasims) might form a cartel to raise their fees. The Hanafi school instructs the qadi to actively forbid such collusion. The underlying principle is to prevent exploitation of the public and ensure fair pricing through competition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the ruling
Determine who is addressed: the qadi (judge) must take action. The ruling imposes an obligation on the qadi.
The qadi is the enforcer of public policy in this context.
2
Identify the prohibited act
The act prohibited is 'shirkah' — here meaning collusive agreement among qasims to fix uniform fees, not a valid partnership.
This is a specific application of the broader prohibition of price-fixing.
3
Understand the rationale
The text gives the reason: 'lest the fee become expensive due to their mutual agreement'. Collusion leads to monopolistic pricing harming the public.
The harm (darar) is the key legal consideration.
4
Contrast with competition
Without collusion, each qasim fears losing the job and offers lower fees, creating a competitive market that benefits the public.
This demonstrates the Hanafi recognition of market forces.
5
Recognize the broader principle
The ruling exemplifies the principle of preventing harm (darar) and promoting public interest (maslahah), which is a foundational objective of Shari'ah.
It also aligns with the maxim 'La darar wa la dirar'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی قاسمین شرکت پر پابندی عائد کر دے قال ولا يترك القاسم يشتركون كيلا تصير الاجرة غالية بتواكلهم وعند عدم الشركة يتبادر كل منهم اليه حيفة الفوت فيرخص الاجر ترجمہ اور نہ چھوڑ بے تقسیم کرنے والوں کو کہ وہ شرکت کریں تا کہ اجرت گراں نہ ہو جائے ان کے اتفاق کرنے کی وجہ سے اور شرکت کے نہ ہونے کے وقت ان میں سے ہر ایک بوارہ کی جانب سبقت کرے گا فوت کے خوف سے تو اجرت ستی رہے گی ۔
The qadi imposes a ban on qasims forming a company. He said: And do not leave the qasims to form a company, lest the fee become expensive due to their mutual agreement, and in the absence of a company, each of them will hasten to it for fear of losing (the opportunity), so the fee becomes cheap. Translation: And do not leave the partitioners (qasims) to form a company, so that the fee does not become expensive due to their agreement, and in the absence of a company, each of them will hasten to the division for fear of loss, so the fee will remain low.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage instructs the qadi to prohibit qasims from forming a syndicate or cartel (shirkah) to fix uniform high fees. The rationale is that if they collaborate, they can demand high fees (ghali). If they are independent and compete, each will hasten to offer his services for fear of losing the job, leading to lower fees (rakhis al-ajr). This ruling aims to protect the public from exploitation.

Key Terms
شرکت (shirkah): Here meaning a collusive agreement among qasims to fix prices, not a valid partnership.
قاسم (qasim): A court-appointed official who divides property among heirs or disputing parties.
اجرة (ajrah): Fee or compensation paid to the qasim for his service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because they are not allowed to make partnerships at all.
C) Because it causes division among them.
D) Because it takes too much time.

Key Takeaway
The qadi must forbid qasims from colluding to fix fees, using his authority to protect public interest and ensure affordable services through competition.

The Judge and the Qasim: Compulsion Prohibited, Mutual Division Allowed
States two rulings on judge's authority over qasims and partners' agreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi rulings regarding the appointment of a qasim and the conditions under which mutual division is valid.

Core Idea
Compulsion in contracts invalidates them; partners may divide by mutual consent unless a minor is involved.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies the limits of a judge's authority in property division. It establishes that judges cannot force co-owners to use a specific qasim (divider) because contracts require free consent, and that co-owners may divide the property themselves unless a minor without a guardian is present. Understanding these principles ensures that property division respects individual autonomy and protects the rights of minors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings stated in the passage
Read the first part: the judge does not compel to a single qasim. Read the second part: partners can divide by mutual agreement, except when a minor is involved.
Focus on the legal outcomes, not just the narrative.
2
Analyze the reasoning for the first ruling
The text gives two reasons: (a) there is no compulsion in contracts, and (b) if only one qasim is designated, they might overcharge. Understand why each reason leads to the prohibition.
The second reason is a practical consequence of monopoly.
3
Analyze the reasoning for the second ruling and its exception
The text states mutual division is valid because owners have full authority over their property. But if a minor is among them, the adult partners have no guardianship (wilayah) over the minor's share; only the judge (or the minor's guardian) can authorize the division.
This highlights the hierarchy of guardianship in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Apply the rulings to a hypothetical scenario
Consider two adult brothers and a minor sister. Can they divide the inherited property by mutual agreement without a judge? Answer: No, because the minor has no guardian among them. The judge must be involved.
If the minor has a father or executor, that guardian replaces the judge.
5
Distinguish between compulsion and mutual agreement
Compulsion invalidates contracts; mutual free consent is essential. The judge's role is to ensure justice, not to force a particular qasim.
This aligns with the general Hanafi principle that contracts require free will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجبر القاضى الناس على قاسم واحد معناه لا يجبرهم على ان يستاجره ولانه لا جبر على العقود ولانه لو تعين لتحكم بالزيادة على اجر مثله ترجمہ اور قاضی لوگوں کو ایک قاسم پر مجبور نہ کرے اسکے معنی ہیں کہ ان کو مجبور نہ کرے اس بات پر کہ وہ اسی کو امیر مقرر کریں اسلئے کہ عقود پر جبر نہیں ہوتا اور اسلئے کہ اگر وہی متعین ہو گیا تو وہ حکام کرے گا زیادتی کے ساتھ اپنے مثل کی اجرت پر ۔ تشریح یعنی قاضی لوگوں کو مجبور نہ کرے کہ اسی قاسم سے بٹوارہ کرائیں کیونکہ یہ جبر علی العقد ہے حالانکہ عقود میں جبر نہیں چلتا۔ اور اگر قاضی ایک ہی کو متعین کرے گا تو وہ اوگوں سے زیادہ اجرت لے گا یہ سمجھتے ہوئے کہ میرے علاوہ تو اور قاسم ہے نہیں ۔ اوگ خو دا تفاق و اتحاد سے تقسیم کر لیں ولو اصطلحوا فاقتموا جاز الا اذا كان فيهم صغير فيحتاج الى امر القاضى لانه لا ولاية لهم عليه ترجمہ اور اگر شر کا اتفاق کرلیں پس آپس میں ہزارہ کر لیں تو جائز ہے مگر جبکہ ان میں کوئی بچہ ہوتو قاضی کے فیصلہ کی جانب حاجت پیش آوے گی اسلئے کہ ان کو ولایت نہیں ہے۔ تشریح اگر شر کا ء خود اتفاق سے تقسیم کر لیں تو جائز ہے لیکن اگر ان میں کوئی بچہ ہو اور اس کا باپ یا وصی نہ ہو تو پھر قاضی کے فیصلہ کی حاجت پیش آئے گی کیونکہ شرکاء کو بچہ پر ولایت نہیں ہے اور قاضی کی ولایت عام ہے۔ اگر بچہ کا نائب ہو تو پھر قضاء قاضی کی حاجت پیش نہیں آئے گی ۔
And the judge shall not compel the people to (use) a single qasim, meaning he shall not compel them to hire him, because there is no compulsion in contracts, and because if he is designated, he would rule with an increase beyond the like of his fee. Translation: And the judge does not compel people to one qasim. Its meaning is that he does not compel them to appoint him as (the agent), because there is no compulsion in contracts, and because if he is designated, he will rule with an increase upon the fee of his like. Commentary: That is, the judge should not compel people to have the division done by that same qasim, because this is compulsion in a contract, whereas compulsion does not apply in contracts. And if the judge designates one person, he will take more fee from them, thinking that besides me there is no other qasim. And if they themselves come to an agreement and divide, it is permissible, except when there is a minor among them, then the judge's decision is needed because they have no guardianship over him. Translation: And if they agree and then divide among themselves, it is permissible, except when there is a minor, then there is need for the judge's order, because they have no guardianship over him. Commentary: If the partners divide by themselves with mutual agreement, it is permissible. But if there is a minor among them and he has no father or executor, then the judge's decision is needed, because the partners have no guardianship over the minor, and the judge's guardianship is general. If the minor has a representative, then the need for the judge's decision does not arise.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from the Hanafi school concerning the appointment of a qasim (divider) for partitioning jointly owned property. First, the judge (qadi) is prohibited from forcing the co-owners to use a single specific qasim. The reasoning is twofold: (a) contracts, including hiring a qasim, require free consent—compulsion invalidates the contract; (b) if only one qasim is designated, he may exploit his monopoly by charging more than the customary fee. Thus, the judge must allow the partners to choose any qualified qasim they wish. Second, if the partners mutually agree and carry out the division themselves without a qasim, it is valid and permissible. However, an exception arises if one of the co-owners is a minor without a guardian (father or executor). In that case, the judge's authorization is necessary because the adult partners have no legal guardianship (wilayah) over the minor's property. If the minor has a guardian (such as a father or appointed executor) who can represent him, then the judge's involvement is not required. This highlights the Hanafi principle that guardianship over a minor's property belongs to the father, then the executor, then the judge, and that co-owners cannot assume that authority.

Key Terms
قاسم (qasim): A person appointed to divide jointly owned property among co-owners.
جبر على العقد (jabr 'ala al-'aqd): Forcing someone to enter into a contract, which is invalid in Islamic law.
ولایت (wilayah): Legal authority to manage the affairs of another, especially a minor or incapacitated person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a judge prohibited from forcing co-owners to use a single qasim?
A) Because qasims are all equally qualified
B) Because compulsion in contracts is invalid and the qasim might overcharge
C) Because the judge lacks authority over property disputes
D) Because co-owners must always divide themselves

Key Takeaway
The judge cannot force a single qasim; partners may divide by mutual agreement unless a minor without guardian is involved.

Judge Prohibiting Qasims from Colluding on Fees
A ruling on judges regulating qasim fees via preventing collusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qasims colluding and explain the public interest reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
The judge must ban qasims from price-fixing to protect the public from high fees.

This short passage from the Kitab al-Qismah of al-Hidayah addresses a practical market regulation issue: qasims (property dividers) could collude to set a minimum fee, harming clients. The Hanafi school gives the judge authority to prohibit such collusion, relying on the principle of preventing harm (darar). The reasoning is economic: competition keeps fees low.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the judge instructed to do? The text says the judge shall not leave the qasims to collude (shirkah). This means prohibition of collusion.
Collusion here means mutual agreement to fix prices.
2
Understand the rationale (illa)
Why is collusion prohibited? Because it leads to high fees (ajrah ghalyah). When qasims agree, they can charge a high fee knowing the client has no alternative.
The illa is the harm of inflated prices.
3
Contrast with the alternative
Without collusion, each qasim hastens to offer services for fear of losing the job. This competition naturally lowers fees, benefiting the public.
Competition is the default desirable state.
4
Extract the legal principle
The ruling shows that the judge has authority to regulate market practices (tas'ir) to prevent exploitation. This is based on maslahah (public interest).
This is a form of siyasah shar'iyyah.
5
Note the manuscript variant
A minor textual note indicates that the word 'qala' (he said) appears in some manuscripts of al-Hidayah but not in Fath al-Qadir. This does not affect the ruling.
Textual variants are common but inconsequential here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يترك القاسم يشتركون كيلا تصير الاجرة غالية بتواكلهم وعند عدم الشركة يتبادر كل منهم اليه حيفة الفوت فيرخص الاجر ترجمہ اور نہ چھوڑ بے تقسیم کرنے والوں کو کہ وہ شرکت کریں تا کہ اجرت گراں نہ ہو جائے ان کے اتفاق کرنے کی وجہ سے اور شرکت کے نہ ہونے کے وقت ان میں سے ہر ایک بوارہ کی جانب سبقت کرے گا فوت کے خوف سے تو اجرت ستی رہے گی ۔ اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ ۱۳۱ كتاب القسمة تشریح سارے قاسمین اکھٹے ہو کر ہوارہ نہ کریں اس کے اوپر قاضی پابندی عائد کر دے ورنہ سب اتفاق کر لیں گے کہ اتنی اجرت ہو گی تو اجرت گراں ہو جائے گی اور جب ان کی شرکت نہ ہوگی تو ہر ایک دوڑے گا کہ کہیں دوسرے قاسم کے پاس نہ چلا جائے تو اس طرح اجرت سستی رہے گی۔ تنبیہ یہاں ہدایہ کے متداول نخوں میں قال ہے۔ فتح القدیر کے نسخہ میں یہاں قال نہیں ہے۔
He said: And he (the judge) shall not leave the qasims to collude (shirkah), lest the fee becomes high due to their mutual agreement. And when there is no collusion, each one of them hastens toward it (the division work) for fear of losing it, so the fee becomes cheap. Translation: And do not leave the dividers to collude, so that the fee does not become expensive due to their agreement. When there is no collusion, each one of them will hasten toward division for fear of losing (the job), so the fee remains cheap. Commentary: All qasims should not divide together; the judge should impose a prohibition on them. Otherwise, they will all agree on a set fee, making it expensive. When they do not collude, each will run (to offer services) lest the client go to another qasim, thus the fee remains low. Note: In the standard manuscripts of al-Hidayah, 'qala' is present; in the Fath al-Qadir copy, 'qala' is not here.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the regulation of qasims (property dividers) by the judge. The judge is instructed not to allow qasims to form a cartel (shirkah) in which they agree collectively on a minimum fee. The rationale is that if they collude, they can charge a high fee because the client has no alternative. However, if collusion is prevented, each qasim competes for the work for fear of losing it to another, which naturally keeps fees low. This ruling reflects the Hanafi concern for public interest (maslahah) and prevention of exploitation. The judge has the authority to regulate the market of qasims to ensure fair pricing. The note (tanbih) indicates a textual variation in manuscripts, but the ruling remains the same.

Key Terms
شرکت (shirkah): Collusion or agreement among qasims to fix prices; a form of partnership that leads to high fees.
اجرة (ajrah): Fee or wage paid to the qasim for his services.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the judge prevent qasims from colluding (shirkah)?
A) To reduce their workload
B) So that competition keeps fees low
C) Because shirkah is always haram
D) To assign all work to one qasim

Key Takeaway
The judge must prohibit qasims from colluding to fix fees, because competition ensures fair pricing while collusion harms the public.

Dispute on Evidence for Partition of Inherited Real Property
Intra-Hanafi dispute on evidence requirement for partition of inherited real property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the requirement of evidence (bayyinah) in inheritance partition cases, and explain the Sahibayn's reasoning based on yad and iqrar.

Core Idea
Possession and acknowledgment suffice for partition unless a denier appears—but Abu Hanifa requires evidence for inherited land.

When heirs come to a judge demanding division of property they claim as inheritance, must they provide formal evidence? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on this point. This lesson explores three scenarios and the Sahibayn's argument that possession (yad) and acknowledgment (iqrar) are sufficient in the absence of a challenger.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage presents three cases: (1) real property claimed as inheritance, (2) movable property claimed as inheritance, (3) real property claimed as purchased. Determine which is disputed.
Only scenario 1 is disputed; the other two are agreed upon.
2
Locate the disputed scenario
Focus on scenario 1: heirs claim a house or land as inheritance. Abu Hanifa requires evidence (bayyinah) of death and number of heirs; the Sahibayn do not.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the judge must not divide until the claimants establish evidence of the deceased's death and the number of heirs.
This is a precaution against potential unknown heirs.
4
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that division is valid based solely on the claimants' acknowledgment, without formal evidence. The judge records the basis to limit the division to the parties.
Their reasoning: possession (yad) indicates ownership, acknowledgment (iqrar) indicates truth, and there is no opponent to necessitate evidence.
5
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that bayyinah is only needed against a denier. Since there is no denier, evidence is futile. The judge may divide and record the basis to protect against future claims.
This is a rational (dalil aqli) argument based on the absence of a challenger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وارث شرکا، قاضی کے پاس آئیں اور اشیاء منقولہ و غیر منقولہ کی تقسیم کا مطالبہ کریں تو قاضی کیلئے کیا حکم ہے،
اقوال فقہاء
قال واذا حضر الشركاء عند القاضى وفى ايديهم دار أو ضيعة وادعوا انهم ورثوها عن فلان لم يقسمها القاضي عند ابي حنيفة حتى يقيموا البيئة على موته وعدد ورثته وقال صاحباه يقسمها باعترافهم ويذكر في كتاب القسمة انه قسمها بقولهم وان كان المال المشترك ما سوى العقار وادعوا انه ميراث قسمه في قولهم جميـ اولو ادعو افى العقار انهم اشتروه قسمه بـ

۱۳۴
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳
ورثا کی تعداد پر گواہ قائم کر دیں اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ اس کو ان کے اعتراف کے مطابق تقسیم کر دے گا اور قسمت کے رجسٹر میں لکھ دے گا کہ اس نے اس کو ان کے قول کے مطابق تقسیم کیا ہے۔ اور اگر مال مشترک زمین کے علاوہ ہو اور وہ دعویٰ کریں کہ یہ میراث ہے تو قاضی ان تمام کے قول کے مطابق اس کو تقسیم کر دے گا اور اگر وہ زمین کے بارے میں دعوی کریں کہ انہوں نے اس کو خریدا ہے تو قاضی اس کو ان کے درمیان تقسیم کر دے گا۔ تشریح یہاں تین مسئلے ہیں ۔
ا۔ شر کا قاضی کے پاس جا کر دعوی کریں کہ یہ فلاں کی میراث ہے ہم کو ملا ہے اور قسمت کا مطالبہ کریں۔
-۲ زمین کے علاوہ اشیاء منقولہ میں سے کسی چیز کے بارے میں یہی دعوی کریں اور قسمت کا مطالبہ کریں۔

اتفاق ہے کہ ان میں اقامت بعینہ کی حاجت نہیں بلکہ بغیر اقامت بینہ کے قاضی اس کو تقسیم کر دے گا ۔ اور پہلا مسئلہ اختلافی ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اقامت بینہ ضروری ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک بغیر اقامت بینہ کے ان کے اقرار کے مطابق بنوارہ کر دیا جائے گا۔ البتہ قاضی یادداشت کی غرض سے تقسیم کے رجسٹر میں درج کرے گا کہ یہ ہوارہ ان کے قول کے موافق کیا گیا ہے۔ تا کہ اگر کوئی اور شریک نکلے تو اس کا نقصان نہ ہو ۔
صاحبین کی دلیل
لهما ان اليد دليل الملك والاقرار امارة الصدق ولا منازع لهم فيقسمه بينهم كما في المنقول الموروث والعقار المشترى وهذا لانه لا منكر ولابينة الاعلى المنكر فلا يفيد الا انه يذكر في كتاب القسمة انه قسمها باقرارهم ليقتصر عليهم ولا يتعداهم

تشریح یہ صاحبین کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ زمین شرکاء کے قبضہ میں ہے جو ملک کی دلیل ہے اور ان کا اقرار ان کے صدق کی علامت ہے اور کوئی ان کا اس دعوئی میں مخالف ہے نہیں تو جیسے صورت ثانیہ اور ثالثہ میں بغیر اقامت بینہ کے بٹوارہ ہوا ہے ایسے یہاں بھی ہونا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ بینہ منکر کے خلاف پیش کرنے کی ضرورت ہوتی ہے اور یہاں کوئی منکر ہے نہیں تو اقامت بینہ لغو ہو جائے گا اسلئے کہ قاضی بغیر اقامت بینہ کے تقسیم کر دے گا مگر تقسیم کے کاغذات میں لکھ دے گا کہ میں نے یہ تقسیم ان کے اقرار پر کی ہے تا کہ یہ تقسیم انہیں تک محدود رہے اور اگر اتفاق سے کوئی اور شریک ہوان تک متعدی نہ ہو سکے۔
The claimant heirs come to the judge and demand division of movable and immovable property; what is the ruling for the judge? Statements of jurists: He (Quduri) said: And when the partners come before the judge, and in their hands is a house or an estate, and they claim that they inherited it from so-and-so, the judge will not divide it according to Abu Hanifa until they establish evidence of his death and the number of his heirs. And the two companions said: He divides it according to their acknowledgment, and he writes in the register of division that he divided it by their statement. And if the joint property is other than real estate and they claim it is inheritance, he divides it according to the statement of all of them. And if they claim regarding real estate that they bought it, he divides it among them. Explanation: Here there are three issues. 1. Partners go to the judge claiming that this is inheritance from so-and-so and they have received it, and demand division. 2. They make the same claim regarding something other than land (movables) and demand division. 3. The issue is regarding land but the claim is not inheritance but purchase. In the last two issues, our three scholars agree that there is no need to present evidence, rather the judge will divide without evidence. And the first issue is disputed. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, presenting evidence is necessary, and according to the Sahibayn, division will be done according to their acknowledgment without evidence. However, the judge will record in the division register that this division was done according to their statement for the purpose of record, so that if another partner appears, there is no harm. The proof of the Sahibayn: For them, possession is evidence of ownership and acknowledgment is a sign of truthfulness, and they have no opponent, so he divides it among them as in inherited movable and purchased real estate. This is because there is no denier, and evidence is only required against the denier, so presenting evidence is not beneficial. However, he writes in the division register that he divided it by their acknowledgment to restrict it to them and not exceed them. Explanation: This is the proof of the Sahibayn, the summary of which is that the land is in the possession of the partners, which is evidence of ownership, and their acknowledgment is a sign of their truthfulness, and there is no opponent to their claim, so just as in the second and third cases division occurred without evidence, so here too it should be. Because evidence is needed to present against the denier, and here there is no denier, so presenting evidence would be futile. Therefore the judge will divide without evidence, but he will write in the division papers that I have made this division based on their acknowledgment, so that this division remains limited to them and cannot extend to another partner if one appears accidentally.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding partition of property claimed as inheritance without formal proof. It states three scenarios: (1) heirs claim real property as inheritance – Abu Hanifa requires witnesses to death and heirs; Sahibayn allow division based on mere claim, with recording. (2) movable property claimed as inheritance – all agree no evidence required. (3) real property claimed as purchased – all agree no evidence required. The Sahibayn's proof is that possession (yad) indicates ownership, acknowledgment (iqrar) indicates truth, and there is no opponent to require evidence. The judge records the basis to limit the division to the parties involved. The text emphasizes that evidence is only needed against a denier.

Key Terms
ید (yad): Possession or control over property; considered a proof of ownership.
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession; here, the heirs' admission of inheritance facts.
بینہ (bayyinah): Formal evidence, typically testimony of two male witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the claimants are trustworthy

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has internal divergence on requiring evidence for inherited property: Abu Hanifa insists on it; the Sahibayn rely on possession and acknowledgment in the absence of a denier.

Partition Prohibited When Absent Heir Has Possession
Ruling that partition is not allowed when the absent heir has possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partition when the absent heir possesses the property and explain the legal reasoning (qada' 'ala al-gha'ib) that prohibits it.

Core Idea
Partition is not allowed when the absent heir holds possession, as it constitutes judgment against an absent person.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario from the Book of Partition (Kitab al-Qismah) in Al-Hidayah: what happens when the property to be divided is actually in the hands of an absent heir or someone holding it for him? The rule is clear: the qadi must not order partition. Why? Because partition would effectively be a judgment against the absent person (qada' 'ala al-gha'ib), which is not permissible in Hanafi law without a representative present. This ruling protects the rights of absentee parties and ensures that possession-based claims are not summarily overridden.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
The text presents three cases: the property is in the hand of (1) the absent heir himself, (2) his depositary (muda'), or (3) a minor. In all three, partition is not allowed.
The key factor is possession (yad) of the absent party or his agent.
2
Extract the legal reason (sabab al-man')
The author states the reason: 'because partition is a judgment against the absent (and the minor) regarding the entitlement of their possession, without a representative present for them.' This is the ilah (effective cause) that triggers the prohibition.
Possession itself creates a right (istihqaq al-yad) that must be defended in court by a proper representative.
3
Understand who counts as a representative
The text distinguishes between a true representative (khasm) and a mere trustee (amin al-khasm). The depositary is not a representative; he only holds the property. Therefore, his presence does not cure the defect.
A guardian or specially appointed agent would be a proper khasm.
4
Evaluate the role of evidence
The ruling holds even if the present parties bring witnesses (bayyinah). The text says: 'In this chapter, there is no difference between establishing evidence and not establishing it; this is the correct view.'
Evidence cannot override the procedural bar of qada' 'ala al-gha'ib.
5
Test the ruling against a counter-argument
One might ask: if the absent heir has no real claim, why not judge quickly? The Hanafi response: possession is a strong proof of right; to disregard it without a representative would be unjust. The rule protects against arbitrary deprivation.
This reasoning aligns with the Hanafi principle of caution in matters of absent parties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان العقار فى يد الوارث الغائب اوشئ منه لم يقسم وكذا اذا كان فى يد مودعه وكذا اذا كان في يد الصغير لان القسمة قضاء على الغائب والصغير باستحقاق يدهما من غير خصم حاضر عنهما وامين الخصم ليس بخصم عنه فيما يستحق عليه والقضاء من غير خصم لا يجوز ولا فرق في هذا الفصل بين اقامة البيئة وعدمها هو الصحيح كما اطلق في الكتاب
ترجمہ اور اگر زمین یا اس کا کچھ حصہ وارث غائب کے قبضہ میں ہو تو قاضی تقسیم نہیں کرے گا اور ایسے ہی جبکہ غائب کے مودع کے پاس ہو اور ایسے ہی جبکہ بچہ کے قبضہ میں ہو اس لئے کہ قسمت قضاء على الغائب والصغیر ہے ان کے قبضہ کے استحقاق کے سلسلہ میں بغیر کسی ایسے خصم کے جو ان دونوں کی جانب سے حاضر ہو اور نصم کا امین غائب کی جانب سے خصم نہیں ہے اس چیز کے اندر جس کا غائب پر استحقاق ثابت کیا جائے اور بغیر خصم کے قضاء جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور اس صورت میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے اقامت بینہ اور اس کے عدم ہے
And if the real estate is in the hand of the absent heir or part of it, he shall not divide. Similarly if it is in the hand of his depositary, and similarly if it is in the hand of a minor, because the partition is a judgment against the absent and the minor regarding the entitlement of their possession without a representative present for them. And the trustee of the opponent (amin al-khasm) is not a representative for him in what is claimed against him. And judgment without a representative is not permissible. In this chapter, there is no difference between establishing evidence and not establishing it; this is correct as is stated in the book.

Translation: And if the land or part of it is in the possession of the absent heir, the qadi will not divide. Similarly if it is in the possession of his depositary, and similarly if it is in the hand of a minor, because the partition is a judgment against the absent and the minor in the context of the entitlement of their possession without any representative present for them. And the trustee of the opponent (amin al-khasm) is not a representative for the absent in what is established against him. And judgment without a representative is not permissible. In this case, there is no difference between establishing evidence and not establishing it; this is the correct view as stated in the book.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Partition. It addresses the scenario where the property (real estate) to be partitioned is physically in the possession of the absent heir, or part of it is, or is in the possession of someone acting on his behalf (like a depositary), or in the possession of a minor. The author rules that the qadi will not order partition in such cases. The reasoning is that partition in such circumstances constitutes a judgment against an absent person (qada' 'ala al-gha'ib) or against a minor, because their possession gives them a right (istihqaq) that needs to be litigated. Since no representative is present for them, the judgment would be invalid. Importantly, the trustee of the opponent (amin al-khasm) — the person who holds the property on trust for the absent party — is not considered a representative for the absent person in this context. Also, there is no difference whether the present parties establish evidence or not; in either case, partition is not permitted. This is stated as the correct position (as-sahih) in the text of Hidayah. The ruling applies to all cases where the absent person has actual or constructive possession, thereby making the partition a judgment against an absent party.

Key Terms
قضاء على الغائب (qada' 'ala al-gha'ib): A judgment passed against an absent person; invalid in Hanafi law without a representative.
امين الخصم (amin al-khasm): Trustee or custodian of the property who holds it for the absent person; not considered a legal representative for litigation.
استحقاق اليد (istihqaq al-yad): The right of possession; the claim to entitlement based on physical control.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where an absent heir's property is in the hand of a depositary (muda'), will the qadi partition the property?
A) Yes, because the depositary can represent the absent heir.
B) No, because the depositary is not a representative for judgment; partition would be qada' 'ala al-gha'ib.
C) Yes, if the present parties provide evidence of their shares.
D) No, but only if the absent heir is not a relative.

Key Takeaway
When an absent heir has possession of the property, partition is prohibited because it constitutes judgment against an absent person, and even evidence cannot override this procedural bar.

12 min
Court Representation and Successorial Ownership
Explaining court representation and milk khalafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between inheritance and purchase cases for representation in court and explain why milk khalafat (successorial ownership) permits representation in the former but not the latter.

Core Idea
Heir's ownership is derivative; buyer's is new – this determines court representation.

In Hanafi law, partition of jointly owned property requires all parties or their representatives present in court. But what if an owner has died or sold their share? The key lies in the nature of ownership: inheritance confers 'successorial ownership' (milk khalafat), enabling the heir to step into the deceased's shoes, while a buyer's ownership is entirely new. This lesson unpacks that distinction and how it affects the permissibility of court-ordered partition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage contrasts inheritance (tawaruth) with purchase (shira). In inheritance, one heir is present and can be appointed as khasm (representative) for the deceased. In purchase, the seller has exited and the present buyer cannot represent the absent co-purchaser.
Both scenarios involve a present and absent party, but the legal treatment differs.
2
Understand the term 'qada ‘ala al-gha’ib'
Judgment against an absent person without a representative is generally invalid in Hanafi law. If partition requires such judgment, it is impermissible. The passage shows inheritance avoids this; purchase does not.
This is a key procedural rule in Hanafi qada.
3
Define milk khalafat
The heir's ownership is not new but derived from the deceased (milk khalafat). This grants the heir the same legal rights and obligations the deceased had regarding the property.
The term 'milk khalafat' is specific to Hanafi fiqh.
4
Examine the proofs
Three proofs show milk khalafat: an heir can return a defective item bought by the deceased; a buyer of the deceased can return a defect to the heir; and the umm walad case where the heir steps into the deceased's shoes for compensation and recovery.
These demonstrate that the heir acts as the deceased's successor.
5
Apply the distinction
Since the heir's ownership is successorial, the present heir can represent the deceased in partition, avoiding qada ‘ala al-gha’ib. In purchase, ownership is new, so the buyer cannot represent the seller's seller, making partition impermissible without the absent party.
This leads to different rulings for inheritance and purchase cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب ... پہلی صورت میں شرکاء میں سے کسی کو میت کی طرف سے خصم مقرر کر لیا جاتا ہے اور یہاں نیابت کی کوئی صورت نہیں بائع تو درمیان سے بالکلیہ خارج ہو چکا ہے اور شریک حاضر کے اندر بھی صلاحیت نہیں ہے کہ وہ شریک غائب کا نائب اور خلیفہ بن جائے تو یہاں قضاء على الغائب لازم آتی ہے اور پہلی صورت میں قضاء علی الغائب نہیں بلکہ متخاصمین کے رو بر وقضاء ہے۔
سوال .. وارث مورث کا خلیفہ کیسے ہے؟ جواب یہ تو بدیہی بات ہے کہ وارث کی ملکیت خلافت کے طریقہ پر ہے جس کی کھلی ہوئی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر مورث نے کوئی چیز خریدی اور مر گیا اور وارث نے اس کے اندر کوئی عیب پایا تو عیب کی وجہ سے اس کو بائع پر واپس کر سکتا ہے۔
اور اسی طرح اگر مورث نے کوئی چیز بیچی اور اس کا انتقال ہو گیا اور مشتری نے اس میں کوئی عیب پایا تو وارث پر عیب کی وجہ سے واپس کر سکتا ہے۔ نیز اسی طرح اگر مورث نے کوئی باندی خریدی اور مر گیا اور وارث نے اس کو ام ولد بنا لیا اور پھر کسی نے استحقاق کا دعویٰ کر دیا تو بچہ تو آزاد ہوگا اور وارث کے اوپر مستحق کیلئے بچہ کی قیمت واجب ہوگی اور باندی کا عقر واجب ہوگا۔ پھر وارث بائع سے بچہ کی قیمت اور باندی کا شمن واپس لے گا اور عقر واپس نہیں لے گا۔ اور اگر مورث خود زندہ ہوتا تو وہ بھی ایسا ہی کرتا جیسے اس کی عدم موجودگی میں وارث نے کیا ہے۔
تو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ وارث کی ملکیت ملک خلافت ہے۔ توارث والے مسئلہ میں یہ صورت تحقیق تھی کہ ان میں سے ایک کو اس مال کے سلسلہ میں جو اس کے قبضہ میں ہے میت کی جانب سے خصم مقرر کر دیا جائے اور دوسرا شریک اپنی جانب سے دوسرے کے مقابلہ میں خصم بنے۔ اس وجہ سے یہ صورت قضاء علی الغائب نہیں ہوئی تھی۔
اور شراء والی صورت قضاء علی الغائب ہوگئی اس وجہ سے اول جائز ہے اور دوسری جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ شراء میں ملک خلافت نہیں بلکہ ملک جدید ہوتی ہے یہی تو وجہ ہے کہ مشتری عیب کی وجہ سے اپنے بائع پر تو واپس کر سکتا ہے مگر بائع کے بائع پر واجب نہیں کر سکتا۔ اس وجہ سے ہم نے ان دونوں میں فرق کیا ہے۔
Answer: In the first case, one of the partners is appointed as adversary (khasm) on behalf of the deceased, and here there is no possibility of representation; the seller has completely exited from the middle, and the present partner also does not have the capacity to become the deputy and successor of the absent partner. So here qada against the absent becomes necessary. In the first case, it is not qada against the absent, but rather judgment is rendered face-to-face between the litigants.
Question: How is the heir the successor (khalifah) of the deceased? Answer: This is intuitive: the heir's ownership is in the manner of succession, and the clear proof is that if the deceased bought something and died, and the heir finds a defect in it, he can return it to the seller due to the defect. Similarly, if the deceased sold something and died, and the buyer finds a defect in it, he can return it to the heir due to the defect. Also, if the deceased bought a slave-girl and died, and the heir made her umm walad, and then someone claimed ownership, then the child will be free, and the heir must pay the value of the child to the claimant, and also the compensation for the slave-girl (adq). Then the heir will recover from the seller the value of the child and the price of the slave-girl, but he will not recover the compensation for the slave-girl. And if the deceased were alive, he would have done exactly what the heir did in his absence.
Thus, it became clear that the heir's ownership is successorial ownership. In the inheritance case, the situation was that one of them was appointed as adversary on behalf of the deceased regarding the property in his possession, and the other partner became the adversary for himself against the other. For this reason, this case was not qada against the absent. The purchase case became qada against the absent, so the first is permissible and the second is not. Because in purchase, ownership is not successorial but new ownership. This is the reason that the buyer can return to his seller due to a defect, but he cannot make the seller's seller liable. For this reason we distinguished between these two.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Qismah (Book of Partition) explains a key legal distinction between two scenarios: when property is inherited versus when it is purchased, and how this affects the possibility of court-ordered partition in the absence of some parties. The author first notes that in the inheritance case (maskalah tawaruth), one of the present heirs can be appointed as the representative (khasm) for the deceased, so there is no need to pass judgment against an absent person (qada 'ala al-gha'ib). In the purchase case, the seller is completely out of the picture, and the present partner cannot represent the absent one, so partition would involve judgment against the absent, which is impermissible. The commentator then addresses a question: how can an heir represent the deceased? The answer establishes the principle of milk khalafat (successorial ownership): the heir steps into the deceased's shoes, inheriting not only the property but also legal rights and duties related to it. Proofs are given: an heir can return a defective item bought by the deceased, and similarly, the buyer of the deceased's property can return a defect to the heir. Additionally, in a case where a slave-girl purchased by the deceased is made umm walad by the heir, and then a third party establishes ownership, the heir must compensate the claimant for the child and the slave-girl, then reclaim the price from the seller—just as the deceased would have done. This shows that the heir's ownership is derivative, not new. Therefore, in inheritance, the heir can represent the deceased as a khasm, making partition possible. In purchase, the buyer's ownership is new (milk jadid), so the buyer cannot represent his seller's seller, and hence partition absent a representative is impermissible.

Key Terms
خصم (khasm): A litigant or adversary in court; here, specifically a person appointed to represent an absent party in a partition lawsuit.
ملک خلافت (milk khalafat): Successorial ownership: the heir's ownership is not original but derived from the deceased, carrying with it the legal standing to act on behalf of the deceased.
قضاء على الغائب (qada 'ala al-gha'ib): Judgment rendered against an absent person who has no representative present in court. Such judgment is generally invalid in Hanafi law except in certain cases.
ملک جدید (milk jadid): New ownership; ownership acquired through purchase or similar transaction, independent of the previous owner's rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the Hanafi ruling that an heir can represent the deceased in a partition lawsuit but a buyer cannot represent the seller?
A) The heir is a blood relative of the deceased.
B) The heir's ownership is successorial (milk khalafat), while the buyer's ownership is new (milk jadid).
C) The buyer did not inherit the property.
D) The seller is no longer alive.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an heir can represent the deceased in court because of milka khalafat, but a buyer cannot represent the seller because their ownership is new and independent.

Judge Cannot Partition When Property is in Possession of Absent Heir, Depositary, or Minor
Ruling on partition when land is in possession of absent party

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three cases where partition is prohibited due to the absence of a representative, and explain the Hanafi reasoning based on the principle that qada' without a khasm is invalid.

Core Idea
Partition requires both parties or their representatives; absence of a khasm blocks partition even if evidence is present.

This lesson examines a procedural rule in Hanafi fiqh: the judge cannot order partition of property when it is in the possession of an absent heir, his depositary, or a minor. The underlying legal principle is that partition constitutes a judgment (qada') against the possessor's right, and valid judgment requires the presence of an adversary (khasm) representing that party. The commentator also resolves an intra-madhhab difference on whether evidence can overcome this procedural bar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited scenarios
State the three situations where partition is not allowed: (a) property in hand of absent heir, (b) property in hand of his depositary, (c) property in hand of a minor.
2
Understand the legal reasoning (dalil)
Grasp why partition is prohibited: it would be judgment against an absent person without a representative, which is invalid.
The principle is 'qada' requires a khasm'.
3
Distinguish the depositary's role
Recognize that the depositary is not a legal representative for litigation; he is only a trustee for safekeeping.
The amin (trustee) is not a khasm.
4
Resolve the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Compare the view of al-Mabsut (allowing partition after evidence) and al-Jami' al-Saghir (disallowing regardless), and note why the latter is preferred.
The author declares the view of al-Jami' al-Saghir as as-sahih.

تشریح یہ صورت پانچویں مسئلہ کا تمہ ہے۔ اس مسئلہ میں جبکہ زمین شرکاء حاضرین کے قبضہ میں تھی ۔ حکم یہ تھا کہ ہؤارہ کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور تمہ میں فرمایا کہ اگر زمین اسی وارث کے قبضہ میں ہے جو غائب ہے ساری اس کے قبضہ میں ہو یا کچھ ہو ۔ یا اس وارث غائب کے مودع کے پاس ہو یاز مین اس وارث کے قبضہ میں ہو جو بچہ ہے۔ تو ان تینوں صورتوں میں خواہ اقامت بیہ ہو یا نہ ہو بہر حال قاضی تقسیم نہیں کرے گا۔ اسلئے کہ غائب اور صغیر کا قبضہ ہے۔ حالانکہ کوئی ان کا مقرر کردہ نائب و وکیل موجود نہیں ہے تو اگر یہاں قسمت کو جائز کر دیا جائے تو بغیر ایسے خصم کے جوان کی جانب سے نائب ہو قضاء لا زم آئے گی اور یہ قضا علی الغائب اور قضاء علی الصغیر ہوگی جو جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور جامع صغیر کا اطلاق بتا رہا ہے کہ اقامت ببینہ میں اور عدم اقامت بعینہ میں یہاں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔ اور اسی روایت کو مصنف نے مبسوط کی روایت کے مقابلہ میں صحیح قرار دیا ہے مبسوط میں کہا ہے کہ اقامت بینہ کے بعد تقسیم کر دی جائے گی۔
سوال... اگر زمین غائب یا صغیر کے قبضہ میں ہو وہاں تو آپ کی دلیل مذکور جاری ہوگی اور جب غائب نے کسی مودع کے پاس رکھی ہو ۔ تو دلیل مذکور جاری نہ ہوگی کیونکہ یہاں مودع غائب کی جانب سے خصم بن سکتا ہے؟
جواب ... یه مودع وامین حفاظت کا ذمہ دار ہے گوئی اس کے اوپر استحقاق کا دعوی کرے اس سلسلہ میں وہ خصم نہیں بن سکتا۔ کیونکہ اس کے پاس یہ ودیعت حفاظت کیلئے ہے نہ کہ ایسا خصم بن کر استحقاق غیر ثابت کرانے کیلئے۔
And if the property or part of it is in the hand of the absent heir, the judge will not partition; likewise if it is in the hand of his depositary; likewise if it is in the hand of a minor. Because partition is qada against the absent and the minor regarding the entitlement of their possession without any adversary (khasm) present on their behalf. And the bailee (amin) of the custodian is not an adversary for him regarding what is claimed against him. And judgment without an adversary is not permissible. And there is no difference in this chapter between establishing evidence and not doing so - this is the correct view, as stated absolutely in the book (al-Jami' al-Saghir).
Translation: And if the land or part of it is in the possession of the absent heir, then the judge will not partition; similarly, when it is with the depositary of the absent; similarly, when it is in the possession of a child. Because partition is qada against the absent and the minor regarding the entitlement of their possession without any adversary who is present on behalf of both, and the amin of the custodian is not an adversary for the absent in the matter for which entitlement is established against him. And judgment without an adversary is not permissible. And in this case, there is no difference between establishing evidence and its absence - this is the correct view, as stated absolutely in the book (al-Jami' al-Saghir).
Explanation: This case is the preamble to the fifth issue. In that issue, when the land was in the possession of the present partners, the ruling was that it would be partitioned. And in the preamble, it is said that if the land is in the possession of the same heir who is absent - whether all of it or part of it - or it is with the depositary of that absent heir, or the land is in the possession of the heir who is a child, then in these three cases, whether evidence is established or not, the judge will not partition. Because it is the possession of the absent and the minor, while there is no appointed deputy or agent for them. So if partition were allowed here, it would entail judgment without a deputy who is an adversary on their behalf, and this would be qada against the absent and qada against the minor, which is not permissible. And the absolute statement of al-Jami' al-Saghir indicates that there is no difference between establishing evidence and not establishing it in this case. And the author has declared this narration correct as opposed to the narration in al-Mabsut, which said that after establishing evidence, partition would be done.
Question: If the land is in the possession of the absent or minor, your mentioned proof applies; but when the absent has placed it with a depositary, the proof does not apply because the depositary can become an adversary on behalf of the absent?
Answer: This depositary is a trustee responsible for safekeeping; if someone claims entitlement against him, he cannot be an adversary in that matter. Because the deposit is with him for safekeeping, not for him to become an adversary and prove the entitlement of someone else.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling about court-ordered partition (qismah) when the property to be divided is in the possession of an absent party. The author states three specific scenarios: (1) the property is in the hand of the absent heir himself; (2) it is with a depositary (mudi') appointed by the absent heir; (3) it is in the hands of a minor heir. In all three cases, the judge cannot order partition, even if evidence of ownership is presented. The reason is that partition in these cases would constitute judgment against the absent or minor regarding their right of possession, but there is no representative (khasm) present to defend their interests. The depositary, even if present, is merely a custodian (amin) and not authorized to act as a litigant for the absent owner. Therefore, the condition for valid judgment—presence of both parties or their representatives—is not met. The commentator then addresses a nuance: there is a difference of narration between al-Mabsut and al-Jami' al-Saghir. In al-Mabsut, it is reported that if evidence is established, partition may proceed. However, the author (likely the author of al-Hidayah or the commentator) adopts the view of al-Jami' al-Saghir, which states that establishing evidence makes no difference; partition is still impermissible. This is the correct view (as-sahih).

Key Terms
مودع (mudi'): The person with whom the property is deposited for safekeeping; a depositary. In this context, the depositary of the absent heir who holds the property on his behalf.
بینہ (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females, etc. Here, evidence that would prove ownership or entitlement.
قضاء على الغائب (qada 'ala al-gha'ib): Judgment rendered against a person who is not present in court and has no representative. This is generally invalid in Hanafi fiqh.
خصم (khasm): An adversary or representative in court who can defend the interests of a party. In this context, the absent or minor heir lacks a khasm, so partition is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The judge cannot partition property that is in the possession of an absent heir, his depositary, or a minor without a representative, even if evidence is presented.

Why Court-Ordered Partition Requires Two Heirs as Adversaries
Ruling with proof on procedural necessity for two litigants in partition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a single heir cannot be both plaintiff and defendant in partition cases and explain the rational proof behind it.

Core Idea
A single heir cannot be both plaintiff and defendant; two present heirs are essential for a valid court-ordered partition.

This lesson examines a key procedural requirement in Hanafi partition law: the necessity of two present heirs as litigants. Even if one heir provides evidence, the judge cannot partition because one person cannot occupy both sides of a lawsuit. We will explore the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling
Identify the act (court-ordered partition) and the condition (at least two present heirs). The passage states: 'If one heir is present, the judge will not partition, even if he establishes evidence.'
The ruling is absolute: no partition with a single heir, regardless of evidence.
2
Understand the Rational Proof
The proof is rational (dalil aqli). The judge needs two litigants to have a valid lawsuit. One person cannot be both the one who sues (mukhasim) and the one being sued (mukhasam). Similarly, one cannot be both the divider (muqasim) and the dividee (muqassam).
This is a procedural requirement; the judge cannot act as both parties.
3
Distinguish from the Permissible Scenario
The passage contrasts with the case where two heirs are present. When two are present, they naturally serve as plaintiff and defendant, making partition procedurally valid.
The exception is not an exception but the normal situation.
4
Apply the Ruling to a Scenario
Imagine one heir appears in court with all ownership documents and witnesses. According to Hanafi law, the judge must still dismiss the partition request until another heir is present.
This ensures procedural fairness; the absent heir's rights are preserved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان حضر وارث واحدلم يقسم وان اقام البينة لانه لابد من حضور خصمين لان الواحد لا يصلح مخاصما ومخاصما وكذا مقاسما ومقاسما بخلاف ما اذا كان الحاضر اثنين على ما بينا
ترجمہ اور اگر ایک وارث حاضر ہوا تو قاضی تقسیم نہیں کرے گا اگر چہ وہ بینہ قائم کر دے اسلئے کہ دو مضموں کا حاضر ہونا ضروری ہے اسلئے کہ ایک شخص مخاصم اور مخاصم اور ایسے ہی مقائم اور مقاسم بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ حاضر دو ہوں اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔
تشریح یہ بھی تمہ مذکورہ کا جزو ہے کہ اگر صرف ایک ہی وارث حاضر ہو اور اقامت بینہ بھی کر دے تب بھی قاضی بٹوارہ نہیں کرے گا۔ زمین اسکے قبضہ میں ہو یا غیر کے کیونکہ فیصلہ کیلئے کم از کم دو شریک حاضر ہونا ضروری ہے اسلئے کہ ایک ہی شخص مخاصم بھی ہو اور مخاصم بھی اور وہی مقاسم بھی ہو اور مقاسم بھی ، یہ نہیں ہوسکتا اسلئے یہاں بنوارہ نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔
He said: And if one heir is present, the judge will not partition, even if he establishes evidence, because the presence of two adversaries is necessary. For one person cannot serve as both plaintiff and defendant, and similarly as both divider and dividee. Unlike the case when two are present, as we have explained.
Translation: And if one heir is present, the judge will not partition, even if he presents evidence, because the presence of two litigants is necessary. For one person is not fit to be both adversary and the one being adversarial against, and similarly both divider and the one being divided with. Unlike the case when two are present, as per the detail we have explained.
Explanation: This is also part of the aforementioned preamble. If only one heir is present and he also presents evidence, even then the judge will not partition, whether the land is in his possession or in someone else's. Because for a decision, at least two partners need to be present. For the same person cannot be both plaintiff and defendant, and the same person cannot be both divider and dividee. This is not possible, so partition cannot be done.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage explains a further condition for court-ordered partition: there must be at least two present heirs who can serve as litigants. If only one heir is present, the judge cannot order partition even if that heir presents full evidence of ownership. The reason is fundamental to procedural law: a single person cannot simultaneously act as the plaintiff (mukhasim) and the defendant (mukhasam), nor can he be the one demanding division and the one being divided upon. A valid lawsuit requires two opposing parties. This is contrasted with the case where two heirs are present, where they can naturally play the roles of plaintiff and defendant. The ruling applies regardless of who holds possession of the property, because the issue is the presence of two adversarial parties, not the location of the property. This passage is part of the same discussion from Kitab al-Qismah, continuing the theme that procedural fairness cannot be sacrificed even for the convenience of partition.

Key Terms
مخاصم ومخاصم (mukhasim wa mukhasam): The one who brings a lawsuit (plaintiff) and the one against whom the lawsuit is brought (defendant). One person cannot be both simultaneously.
مقاسم ومقاسم (muqasim wa muqassam): The one who demands division (divider) and the one with whom property is divided (dividee). Again, a single person cannot play both roles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the judge not partition when only one heir is present, even if that heir presents evidence?
A) Because evidence from one person is insufficient under Hanafi law.
B) Because one person cannot be both plaintiff and defendant in the same case.
C) Because the absent heir's consent is not given.
D) Because the property must be in the possession of the present heir.

Key Takeaway
A court-ordered partition requires two present heirs as adversaries; one person cannot fill both roles.

Judge Appoints Guardian for Minor Heir in Partition
Ruling on partition with minor and adult heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partition when a minor heir is present and identify the role of the guardian appointed by the judge.

Core Idea
A minor cannot litigate, so the judge appoints a guardian to represent him in partition.

In inheritance partition, all co-owners must be present as litigants. But a minor lacks legal capacity. How can partition proceed? The Hanafi school solves this by allowing the judge to appoint a guardian (wasi) for the minor, who acts as the minor's representative. This lesson examines the basic ruling and its condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
The scenario involves two present heirs: one minor and one adult. The adult can represent himself, but the minor cannot.
Minor here means a child who has not reached puberty (bulugh).
2
Recognize the legal barrier
A minor cannot be a litigant in court (qada). Without a representative, partition cannot take place because there must be two adversaries.
Hanafi law requires two litigants for a lawsuit; a minor alone cannot sue or defend.
3
State the judge's action
The judge (qadi) appoints a wasi (guardian) specifically for this case to represent the minor. Then the judge proceeds with partition.
The wasi is often a trustworthy relative or a neutral third party.
4
Note the condition of evidence
The passage says 'when evidence is established' (idha uqimat al-bayyinah). This means the claim of inheritance or ownership must be proven before partition.
This condition ensures that the partition is based on a valid right.
5
Understand the continuation
The text is cut off at 'wa kadha idha' (and also if...). The full ruling likely covers a second scenario where evidence is not required, perhaps when the property is already jointly owned without dispute.
For a complete understanding, refer to al-Hidayah or a full sharh.

Source Text

ولو كان الحاضر صغيراً وكبيراً نصب القاضى عن الصغير وصيا و قسم اذا اقيمت البيئة وكذا اذا
And if the present person is a minor and an adult, the judge appoints a guardian (wasi) for the minor and partitions, when evidence is established, and also when...
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage begins a new sub-section: when the present heirs consist of a minor and an adult, the judge can proceed with partition after appointing a guardian (wasi) for the minor. The minor, being legally incapacitated, cannot act as a litigant. However, the judge can appoint a guardian to represent the minor's interests, thereby fulfilling the requirement for two adversaries. The condition 'when evidence is established' indicates that the claim to the property must be proven. The text is incomplete, but it likely continues to state the second scenario where evidence is not needed (based on similar passages in the Hidayah). The appointment of a guardian is a standard Hanafi mechanism to enable legal proceedings involving minors.

Key Terms
وصی (wasi): A guardian appointed by the judge to represent a minor in legal matters, including litigation and property division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The minor's age
B) The existence of a blood relative guardian
C) Evidence of ownership
D) Consent of the adult heir

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school enables partition with a minor heir by having the judge appoint a guardian (wasi) and requiring proof of ownership before proceeding.
