Partition Prohibited When Absent or Minor Holds Property
Ruling on partition when property is held by absent or minor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partition when property is in the possession of an absent or minor heir, explain the rationale based on the prohibition of judgement against an absent/minor, and distinguish the preferred narration (al-Jami' al-Saghir) from the alternative (al-Mabsut).

Core Idea
Partition is prohibited when the absent or minor holds possession, because it would be a judgement without a representative.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in the law of partition (qismat) under Hanafi fiqh. When co-owned property is in the possession of an absent heir or a minor, the judge is not permitted to order partition, even if the present heirs provide evidence. The reason is that the absent or minor has no representative in court, and a ruling against them would be invalid. The author explains the rationale and resolves an intra-school disagreement between two narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List the three situations where the judge cannot partition: (1) land in possession of the absent heir, (2) land held by the absent heir's depositary, (3) land in possession of a minor heir.
2
Understand the legal reason (illah)
The prohibition stems from the absence of a representative (nā'ib) for the absent or minor who can act as an opponent in court. Partition would require a judgement against them without proper representation.
This is a manifestation of the principle 'qaḍā' 'alā al-ghā'ib' being impermissible.
3
Compare the two narrations
The passage contrasts the absolute prohibition in al-Jami' al-Saghir with the permission in al-Mabsut (partition allowed after evidence). The author prefers the former.
The tarjīḥ is based on authority weight (Zahir al-Riwayah) and the principle of avoiding doubtful judgements.
4
Address the objection about the depositary
A question arises: could the depositary (muda') not serve as opponent? The answer is no, because he is only a trustee for safekeeping, not authorized to litigate ownership.
The depositary's role is limited to preservation; he cannot be dragged into a dispute over entitlement.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Test your understanding: if an absent heir has left the land with a lessee (musta'jir), does the same prohibition apply? Consider whether the lessee can be considered an opponent.
Hint: the lessee has a contractual relationship but is not a representative for ownership claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کے درمیان یہی صحیح ہے جیسا کہ کتاب ( جامع صغیر) میں مطلق فرمایا ہے۔
تشریح یہ صورت پانچویں مسئلہ کا تمہ ہے۔ اس مسئلہ میں جبکہ زمین شرکاء حاضرین کے قبضہ میں تھی ۔ حکم یہ تھا کہ ہؤارہ کر دیا جائے گا۔
اور تمہ میں فرمایا کہ اگر زمین اسی وارث کے قبضہ میں ہے جو غائب ہے ساری اس کے قبضہ میں ہو یا کچھ ہو ۔ یا اس وارث غائب کے مودع کے پاس ہو یاز مین اس وارث کے قبضہ میں ہو جو بچہ ہے۔ تو ان تینوں صورتوں میں خواہ اقامت بیہ ہو یا نہ ہو بہر حال قاضی تقسیم نہیں کرے گا۔ اسلئے کہ غائب اور صغیر کا قبضہ ہے۔ حالانکہ کوئی ان کا مقرر کردہ نائب و وکیل موجود نہیں ہے تو اگر یہاں قسمت کو جائز کر دیا جائے تو بغیر ایسے خصم کے جوان کی جانب سے نائب ہو قضاء لا زم آئے گی اور یہ قضا علی الغائب اور قضاء علی الصغیر ہوگی جو جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور جامع صغیر کا اطلاق بتا رہا ہے کہ اقامت ببینہ میں اور عدم اقامت بعینہ میں یہاں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔ اور اسی روایت کو مصنف نے کو مبسوط کی روایت کے مقابلہ میں صحیح قرار دیا ہے مبسوط میں کہا ہے کہ اقامت بینہ کے بعد تقسیم کر دی جائے گی۔ سوال... اگر زمین غائب یا صغیر کے قبضہ میں ہو وہاں تو آپ کی دلیل مذکور جاری ہوگی اور جب غائب نے کسی مودع کے پاس رکھی ہو ۔ تو دلیل مذکور جاری نہ ہوگی کیونکہ یہاں مودع غائب کی جانب سے خصم بن سکتا ہے؟ جواب ... یه مودع وامین حفاظت کا ذمہ دار ہے گوئی اس کے اوپر استحقاق کا دعوی کرے اس سلسلہ میں وہ خصم نہیں بن سکتا۔ کیونکہ اس کے پاس یہ ودیعت حفاظت کیلئے ہے نہ کہ ایسا خصم بن کر استحقاق غیر ثابت کرانے کیلئے۔
The correct view among these is as stated absolutely in al-Jami' al-Saghir. Explanation: This is the preface to the fifth issue. In this issue, when the land was in possession of the present partners, the ruling was that it would be partitioned. And in the preface it is stated that if the land is in the possession of the heir who is absent, either all of it or part of it; or it is with the depositary (muda') of the absent heir; or the land is in the possession of the heir who is a child; then in these three cases, whether evidence is established or not, in any case the judge will not partition. Because it is the possession of the absent and the minor, while there is no appointed deputy or agent present on their behalf. If partition were allowed here, a judgement would be necessitated without an opponent who is a deputy on their behalf, and this would be judgement against the absent and judgement against the minor, which is not permissible. And the absolute wording of al-Jami' al-Saghir indicates that there is no difference between establishing evidence and not establishing evidence in this case. And the author has deemed this narration correct as opposed to the narration in al-Mabsut, which says that partition will be done after establishing evidence. Question: If the land is in the possession of the absent or minor, then your mentioned argument applies; and when the absent has placed it with a depositary, then the mentioned argument does not apply because here the depositary can act as an opponent on behalf of the absent? Answer: This depositary is only responsible for safekeeping; if someone claims entitlement over him, he cannot become an opponent in that matter because the deposit with him is for safekeeping, not for him to become an opponent to prove the entitlement of others.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on partition when the property is held by an absent heir or a minor. The text clarifies that in three scenarios—when the land is in the possession of the absent heir, when it is with the absent heir's depositary, or when it is in the possession of a minor heir—the judge must not partition, regardless of whether the present heirs produce evidence. The reason is that the absent and minor have possession but no representative present to act as an opponent in court. Partition would constitute a judgement against an absent person or a minor, which is prohibited according to Hanafi principle. The author prefers the ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir over that of al-Mabsut, which allowed partition after evidence was established. A question arises about the depositary: could he not serve as opponent? The answer is no, because the depositary is only a trustee for safekeeping; he is not empowered to engage in litigation to prove ownership claims. Thus the prohibition remains.

Key Terms
قسمت (qismat): Division or partition of jointly owned property among co-owners.
خصم (khasm): An opponent in a legal dispute; a party to a lawsuit.
قضاء علی الغائب (qada' 'ala al-gha'ib): Judgement against an absent person without representation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The judge must partition the land.
B) The judge may partition only if the absent heir's depositary agrees.
C) The judge cannot partition the land at all.
D) The judge partitions only after one year.

Key Takeaway
A judge must not order partition of jointly owned property when the property is in the possession of an absent or minor heir who has no legal representative, even if evidence is presented.

Partition Requires Two Opposing Parties
Ruling that partition requires at least two opposed parties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that partition is invalid with only one heir present and explain the requirement of two opposing parties.

Core Idea
One person cannot be both plaintiff and defendant – partition needs two opponents.

This lesson addresses a fundamental procedural requirement in Hanafi inheritance partition (qisma). Even if a single heir presents irrefutable evidence, the judge must not proceed unless at least two heirs are present. Why? Because a legal dispute requires two distinct parties: one cannot simultaneously be the claimant and the respondent. This rule safeguards the adversarial nature of judicial proceedings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the matn: what does the judge do when only one heir is present? The ruling is clear: he does not partition, even if evidence is established.
The ruling applies regardless of who holds possession of the property.
2
Locate the Proof (Dalil)
The proof is rational (aqli): the text states 'because the presence of two opponents is necessary since one person cannot be both plaintiff and defendant.'
No Quran or hadith is cited; the proof is inherent in the nature of legal proceedings.
3
Understand the Rationale
Why can't one person be both? Because a valid lawsuit requires a claimant (mukhasim) and a respondent (mukhasam). Similarly, partition requires a person seeking division (muqasim) and a person against whom division is sought (muqasam). These roles cannot be combined.
The same logic applies to both litigation (mukhasama) and partition (muqasama).
4
Contrast with Two Heirs Present
The exception: when two heirs are present, partition is valid because both roles are filled. This is the normal case, as explained earlier in the text.
The rule is not about the number of heirs in total, but about the number present before the judge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک وارث حاضر ہو تو قاضی تقسیم نہیں کرے گا اگر چہ وہ بعینہ قائم کر دے
قال وان حضر وارث واحدلم يقسم وان اقام البينة لانه لابد من حضور خصمين لان الواحد لا يصلح مخـاصـمـا ومـخـاصـمـا وكــذا مـقـاسـمـا ومـقـاسـمـا بـخـلاف ما اذا كـان الـحـاضـر اثنين على ما بينا

تشریح یہ بھی تمہ مذ کورہ کا جزو ہے کہ اگر صرف ایک ہی وارث حاضر ہو او را قامت بینہ بھی کر دے تب بھی قاضی بٹوارہ نہیں کرے گا۔ زمین اسکے قبضہ میں ہو یا غیر کے کیونکہ فیصلہ کیلئے کم از کم دو شریک حاضر ہونا ضروری ہے اسلئے کہ ایک ہی شخص مخاصم بھی ہو اور مخاصم بھی اور وہی مقاسم بھی ہو اور مقاسم بھی ، یہ نہیں ہوسکتا اسلئے یہاں بنوارہ نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔
If one heir is present, the judge will not partition, even if he establishes evidence. He said: If one heir is present, he will not partition, even if he establishes evidence, because the presence of two opponents is necessary since one person cannot be both plaintiff and defendant, and similarly cannot be both one who partitions and one against whom partition is made. Unlike when two are present, as we have explained. Translation: And if one heir is present, the judge will not partition even if he establishes evidence, because the presence of two opponents is necessary; one person cannot be plaintiff and defendant, nor can he be the one who partitions and the one against whom partition is made. Contrary to when two are present, according to the detail we have explained. Explanation: This is also part of the aforementioned preface: if only one heir is present and he establishes evidence, still the judge will not partition, whether the land is in his possession or not, because for a decision at least two partners must be present; one person cannot be both plaintiff and defendant and also the one who partitions and the one against whom partition is made. This is not possible, so partition cannot be done here.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning partition when only one heir is present. The matn states that even if a single heir establishes clear evidence, the judge must not partition. The reason provided is that two parties are required for a valid legal proceeding: one person cannot simultaneously act as plaintiff and defendant, nor as the one demanding partition and the one resisting it. The commentary emphasizes that this applies regardless of whether the land is in that heir's possession or not. The necessity of two opponents (khasmayn) is a fundamental requirement in Hanafi court procedure for partition cases.

Key Terms
مخاصم (mukhasim): One who engages in litigation; a plaintiff or defendant.
مقاسم (muqasim): One who participates in partition; a party in the division of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A judge must never partition inherited property when only one heir is present, because legal proceedings require two opposing parties.

Partition When Minor and Adult Heir Present
Ruling on partition with minor/adult or legatee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a judge may partition an estate when a minor and an adult heir are present, and apply the requirement of two opposing parties.

Core Idea
Partition requires two opposing parties; a guardian stands in place of a minor to satisfy this requirement.

In Hanafi inheritance law, partition requires two adversaries. When one heir is a minor, the judge must appoint a guardian to represent him. This lesson examines two scenarios: a minor with an adult heir, and an adult heir with a legatee. The key principle is that the guardian's presence is legally equivalent to the minor's own presence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognize that the passage covers two cases: (1) a minor and an adult heir, (2) an adult heir and a legatee of one-third.
2
Identify the condition of two opponents
Partition requires two opposing parties (khism). Without them, the judge cannot proceed.
3
Explain the judge's role in appointing a guardian
When a minor is involved, the judge must appoint a guardian (wasi) to act as the minor's opponent.
4
Explain the principle of qiyam maqam
The guardian stands in the place of the minor, making the minor's presence effective as if he were an adult.
5
Note the evidentiary requirement
In both cases, evidence (bayyinah) of inheritance or bequest must be established before partition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ور ناصغیر اور کبیر ہوں تو قاضی صغیر کی جانب سے وصی مقرر کر کے تقسیم کر دے
ولو كان الحاضر صغيراً وكبيراً نصب القاضى عن الصغير وصيا و قسم اذا اقيمت البيئة وكذا اذا حضروارث كبير وموصى له بالثلث فيها فطلبا القسمة واقاما البينة على الميراث والوصية تقسمه الاجتماع الخصمين الكبير عن الميت والموصى له عن نفسه وكذا الوصى عن الصبى لأنه حضر بنفسه بعد البلوغ
لقيامه مقامه
ترجمہ اور اگر حاضر صغیر اور کبیر ہو تو قاضی صغیر کی جانب سے ایک وصی مقرر کر دے گا اور تقسیم کر دے گا جبکہ بینہ قائم کر دیا گیا ہو اور ایسے ہی جبکہ وارث کبیر اور اس کے گھر کے اندر جس کو ثاث کی وصیت کی گئی حاضر ہوں اور دونوں میراث اور وصیت پر گواہ قائم کر دیں تو قاضی اس کو تقسیم کر دے گا۔ دو خصموں کے جمع ہو جانے کی وجہ سے کبیر میت کی جانب سے اور موصی لڑ اپنی جانب سے اور ایسے ہی وہی بچہ کی جانب سے گویا کہ بلوغ کے بعد خود حاضر ہوا ہو۔ وصی کے بچہ کے قائم مقام ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح اگر دو وارث حاضر ہو گئے مگر ان میں سے ایک بچہ ہے اور ایک بالغ ہے یا ان میں سے ایک بالغ اور دوسرا وہ ہے جس کیلئے میت نے تہائی کی وصیت کر رکھی ہے تو قاضی کیا کرے۔
تو فرمایا کہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں قاضی تقسیم کر دے گا۔ مگر اقامت بعینہ دونوں میں شرط ہے۔ اور پہلی صورت میں یہ بھی شرط ہے کہ قاضی بچہ کی طرف سے کسی وصی کو مقرر کر دے۔ اب دونوں صورتوں میں حصسمین کا اجتماع ہو گیا جو قضاء کیلئے شرط ہے۔ پہلی صورت میں بالغ کو میت کی جانب سے خصم مانا جائے گا اور وصی کو بچہ کی طرف سے اور دوسری صورت میں بالغ میت کی طرف سے اور موصی لہ بالٹنٹ اپنی طرف سے ۔ چونکہ وصی بچہ کا قائم مقام ہے تو وصی کا حاضر ہونا ایسا ہے گویا کہ بچہ بلوغ کے بعد خود ہی حاضر ہو گیا۔
And if a minor and an adult are present, the judge will appoint a guardian for the minor and partition when evidence is established. Similarly, if an adult heir and a legatee of one-third are present in the house, and both demand partition and establish evidence on inheritance and the bequest, the judge will partition it due to the meeting of two opponents: the adult on behalf of the deceased, the legatee on his own behalf, and likewise the guardian on behalf of the child, as if the child himself had appeared after reaching majority because the guardian stands in his place. Translation: And if a minor and an adult are present, the judge will appoint a guardian for the minor and will partition when evidence is established. Similarly, if an adult heir and one to whom one-third was bequeathed are present and both demand partition after establishing evidence on inheritance and bequest, the judge will partition it due to the gathering of two opponents: the adult on behalf of the deceased, the legatee on his own behalf, and similarly the guardian on behalf of the child, as if he had appeared himself after adulthood because the guardian stands in his place. Explanation: If two heirs are present but one is a child and the other an adult, or one is an adult and the other is one to whom the deceased bequeathed one-third, what should the judge do? It was said that in both cases the judge will partition, but establishing evidence is a condition in both. In the first case, it is also a condition that the judge appoint a guardian for the child. Now in both cases, two opponents have gathered, which is a condition for judgement. In the first case, the adult is considered an opponent on behalf of the deceased, and the guardian on behalf of the child. In the second case, the adult is on behalf of the deceased and the legatee on his own behalf. Since the guardian stands in the place of the child, the presence of the guardian is as if the child had appeared himself after reaching adulthood.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling when a minor and an adult heir are present, or when an adult heir and a legatee of one-third are present. In both cases, the judge can partition provided evidence is established. In the first case, the judge must appoint a guardian (wasi) for the minor; then the adult acts as opponent on behalf of the deceased, and the guardian on behalf of the minor. In the second case, the adult acts on behalf of the deceased, and the legatee on his own behalf. The key point is that two opponents must be present for a valid partition. The guardian's standing in place of the minor makes the minor's presence effective as if he were an adult. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that a guardian can represent a minor in legal proceedings to meet the requirement of two opposing parties.

Key Terms
وصی (wasi): A guardian appointed by the judge to represent a minor in legal matters.
قیام مقام (qiyam maqam): Standing in place of another; representation by substitution.
موصی لہ بالثلث (musa lahu bil-thuluth): A person to whom one-third of the estate is bequeathed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Appoint a guardian (wasi) for the minor.
C) Seek permission from the absent guardian.
D) Only partition if the minor agrees through a representative.

Key Takeaway
Partition requires two opposing parties; a guardian for a minor serves as one party, enabling the process to proceed without delay.

Ruling on Partition with a Minor Heir or Legatee
Ruling on partition with minor or legatee present.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a qadi must appoint a guardian for a minor and proceed with partition, and apply the ruling to a scenario with an adult heir and a legatee.

Core Idea
The qadi must appoint a guardian for a minor before partition, ensuring all litigants are represented.

In inheritance partition, if one heir is a minor, the qadi cannot simply proceed. The law requires proper representation. This passage from Kitab al-Qisma outlines the procedure: the qadi appoints a guardian (wasi) for the minor, then, upon presentation of evidence, performs the division. The same applies when a legatee is present alongside an adult heir. This ensures that the rights of all parties are protected and that the partition is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties involved
The passage mentions two scenarios: a minor and an adult heir, or an adult heir and a legatee. List the parties and their roles.
2
Determine the qadi's initial obligation
What must the qadi do first regarding the minor? Appoint a guardian (wasi) from the minor's side if none exists.
3
Identify the prerequisite for partition
What must both parties present? Evidence (bayyinah) of inheritance or the will.
4
Understand the representation logic
The adult heir represents the deceased's estate; the legatee represents himself; the guardian represents the minor. Both litigants (khasmin) must be present.
5
Apply to a similar scenario
What if the minor is the only heir? The qadi still must appoint a guardian if partition is sought, because the minor cannot represent himself.

كتاب القسمة
وإذا كان حاضر صغير وكبير فالقاضي ينصب وصيا من جهة الصغير ويقسم إذا أقاما البينة وكذلك إذا كان الوارث كبير والموصى له بالثلث في الدار حاضرا وأقاما البينة على الميراث والوصية يقسم القاضي لجمع الخصمين الكبير عن الميت والموصى له عن نفسه وكذا الوصى عن الصبى لأنه حضر بنفسه بعد البلوغ لقيامه مقامه
Book of Division. And if a minor and a major are present, the qadi appoints a guardian for the minor and divides if they present evidence. Similarly, if the heir is an adult and the legatee of one-third in the house is present and they present evidence on the inheritance and the will, the qadi divides due to the gathering of the two litigants: the adult on behalf of the deceased, the legatee on his own behalf, and likewise the guardian on behalf the child, because he attended himself after puberty due to his standing in his place.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Division (Kitab al-Qisma) states a ruling on partition when one inheritor is a minor (saghir) and another is an adult (kabir), or when the adult heir is present alongside a legatee (musa lahu) who has been bequeathed a third of the property. The qadi must first appoint a guardian (wasi) for the minor if there is none. Then, upon the presentation of evidence (bayyinah) regarding the inheritance and the will, the qadi performs the division. The legal basis is that both parties—the adult heir representing the deceased's estate and the legatee representing himself—are present as litigants (khasmin). The guardian stands in the place of the minor, as if the minor had reached majority and attended personally. This ensures that all necessary parties are present for a valid judicial partition.

Key Terms
وصي (wasi): A guardian appointed by the qadi to represent a minor in legal proceedings.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, usually two witnesses, proving the inheritance or will.
خصمين (khasmin): The two litigants in a partition case: the heir and the legatee/guardian.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Wait until the minor becomes adult
D) Ask the adult heir to represent the minor

Key Takeaway
Proper representation of a minor through a guardian is essential for a valid judicial partition.

Testimony of Partitioners: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on testimony of partitioners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the testimony of partitioners, explain Imam Muhammad's objection, and evaluate the Shaykhayn's response.

Core Idea
Partitioners testify about the partners' receipt, not their own division, so their testimony is accepted.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether partitioners (qasimin) can testify that each partner received his share. Imam Muhammad argues they are testifying about their own act, which is inadmissible. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) counter that they testify about the partners' act of receipt. Understanding this distinction reveals the Shari'a's precision in identifying the subject of testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of testimony
Determine what exactly the partitioners are testifying about according to each side: is it their own act of division or the partners' act of receipt?
Imam Muhammad says they testify about their own act; Shaykhayn say about the partners' act.
2
Examine Imam Muhammad's proof
How does Imam Muhammad analogize to conditional emancipation? What is the illa (effective cause) in that analogy?
The illa is that a person testifies about his own act, which is not accepted.
3
Examine Shaykhayn's proof
How do Shaykhayn distinguish the act of division (tamyiz) from the act of receipt (istifa)? Why is the division not a proper subject for testimony?
Division is not binding before possession; testimony requires a binding act.
4
Compare the positions
What is the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the disagreement? Under which view would partners need additional witnesses?
Under Imam Muhammad, partners need other witnesses; under Shaykhayn, partitioners suffice.
5
Note the special case of qadi-appointed partitioners
According to the note, when is revocation of division possible? How does this affect the binding nature of the division and the testimony?
If qadi appoints, shares become binding immediately; if partners appoint, revocation possible before possession.

امام محمد کی دلیل
لمحمد انهما شهدا على فعل انفسهما فلا تقبل كمن علّق عتق عبده بفعل غيره فشهد ذالك الغير على فعله
ترجمہ محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ انہوں نے اپنے فعل پر گواہی دی ہے تو یہ قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ جیسے وہ شخص جس نے اپنے غلام کے عقیق کو اپنے غیر کے فعل پر معلق کیا ہو۔ پس اس غیر نے اپنے فعل پر گواہی دی۔
تشریح یہ امام محمد کی دلیل ہے کہ یہاں قاسمان اپنے فعل پر گواہی دے رہے ہیں حالانکہ اپنے فعل پر گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوتی ۔ جیسے زید نے کہا کہ اگر خالد نے آج ایک پارہ کی تلاوت کی تو میر اغلام آزاد ہے۔ غلام نے اپنے عشق کا دعوی کیا اور خالد نے ایک پارہ پڑھنے کی گواہی دی تا کہ غلام آزاد ہو جائے تو خالد کی گواہی معتبر نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس نے اپنے فعل پر گواہی دی ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی گواہی غیر مقبول ہوگی ۔
شیخین کی دلیل
ولهما انهـمـا شـهـدا عـلـى فـعـل غـيـرهما وهو الاستيفاء والقبض لا على فعل انفسهما لان فعلهما التمييز ولاحاجة الى الشهادة عليه اولانه لا يصلح مشهوداً به لما انه غير لازم وانما يلزمه بالقبض والاستيفاء وهو فعل الغير فتقبل الشهادة عليه
ترجمہ اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاسموں نے اپنے غیر کے فعل پر گواہی دی ہے اور وہ وصول و قبضہ ہے نہ کہ اپنے فعل پر ۔ اسلئے کہ ان کا فعل جدا کرنا ہے جس پر شہادت کی حاجت نہیں اور اسلئے کہ تمیز مشہور بہ بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا اسلئے کہ یہ لازم نہیں ہے اور لازم ہوگا یہ ( فعل قاسم ) اس کو (ان میں سے ہر ایک کو قبضہ اور وصول کے بعد اور وہ ( وصول و قبضہ ) غیر کا فعل ہے تو اس پر شہادت قبول کی جائے گی۔ تشریح یہ شیخین کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اپنے اس پر گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی یہ تو مسلم ہے مگر یہ اپنے فعل پر گواہی نہیں بلکہ فعل غیر پر ہے کیونکہ قاسمین کا کام ہر ایک کا حصہ الگ الگ کرنا ہے جو وہ کر چکے۔ جس میں مقاسمین میں سے کسی کو اختلاف نہیں ۔ بلکہ اختلاف اپنے حق کو وصول کرنے اور اس پر قابض ہونے میں ہے تو قائمین کی گواہی فعل غیر پر ہوگی۔ لہذا معتبر ہوگی ۔ چونکہ تمیز پر گواہی کی حاجت ہی نہیں ۔ یا یوں کہئے کہ تمیز میں یہ صلاحیت ہی نہیں کہ اسکے اوپر گواہی دی جائے کیونکہ گواہی الزام کیلئے ہوتی ہے اور تمیز میں قبضہ سے پہلے متقاسمین کا رجوع جائز ہے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قبل القبض تمیز لازم نہیں تو وہ مشہور بہ بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ تنبیه مشہور بہ ، جس پر گواہی دی جائے، قائم تقسیم کرنے والا ، متقاسم تقسیم چاہنے والا یعنی شریک جو دلیل پیش کی گئی ہے کہ قبل القبض
رجوع صحیح ہے۔ یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ تقسیم شرکاء کی رضا مندی سے ہو رہی ہو اور جب تقسیم کرنے والا قاضی یا اس کا نائب ہو تو حصوں کے نکلنے کے بعد شرکاء میں سے کسی کو انکار کا حق نہ ہوگا۔
Whether the partitioners are appointed by the qadi or hired by the partners themselves, both are equal. That is, in any case, the ruling on the testimony of the partitioners is as mentioned. Imam Muhammad's proof: For Muhammad, they testified about their own act, so it is not accepted, like one who conditions the freeing of his slave upon the act of another, and that other testifies about his own act. Translation: Muhammad's proof is that they testified about their own act, so it will not be accepted. Explanation: This is Imam Muhammad's proof that here the partitioners are testifying about their own act, whereas testimony about one's own act is not accepted. For example, Zaid said, 'If Khalid recites one juz today, my slave is free.' The slave claimed his emancipation, and Khalid testified that he recited one juz so that the slave would be freed. Khalid's testimony is not acceptable because he testified about his own act. Similarly, here the testimony will not be accepted. The proof of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): And for them, they testified about the act of others, which is receipt and possession, not about their own act. Because their act is the division (tamyiz), and there is no need for testimony about it, and because it is not suitable as that which is testified about since it is not binding. It becomes binding only with possession and receipt, which are the acts of others. So testimony about it is accepted. Translation: The proof of the two shaykhs is that the partitioners testified about the act of others, which is receipt and possession, not about their own act. Because their act is separation, for which testimony is not needed. Explanation: This is the proof of the two shaykhs, the summary of which is that testimony about one's own act is not accepted, that is agreed. But here they are not testifying about their own act, rather about the act of others, because the partitioners' work is to separate the shares for each, which they have done. There is no dispute among the partners about that. Rather, the dispute is about receiving one's right and taking possession of it. So the partitioners' testimony is about the act of others, hence it will be credible. Since there is no need for testimony about the division. Or because the division does not have the capacity to be testified about, because testimony is for establishing liability, and before possession, the partners may revoke the division, which shows that before possession the division is not binding, so it cannot be that which is testified about. Note: That which is testified about; qasim: the divider; mutaqasim: the one seeking division, i.e., the partner. The proof given that revocation before possession is valid applies when the division is done with the consent of the partners. When the divider is the qadi or his deputy, after the shares are determined, none of the partners has the right to refuse.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the admissibility of testimony given by the two partitioners (qasimin) about the division of property. The issue is: when the partitioners (appointed by the qadi or hired by the partners) testify that each partner has received his share, is their testimony accepted? Imam Muhammad argues that they are testifying about their own act (the division), which is not admissible. He draws an analogy with someone who conditionally frees his slave upon another's act, and that other testifies to his own act. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that the partitioners are testifying about the act of others (the receipt and possession), not their own act. Their own act is merely the division (tamyiz), which does not require testimony. Since the division is not binding before possession, it cannot be subject to testimony. The receipt is the act of the partners. Hence testimony about receipt is admissible. They also note that testimony is for establishing liability (ilzam), and division before possession is revocable, so it is not a proper subject for testimony. Therefore, the testimony is accepted. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of the Shaykhayn.

Key Terms
قاسم (qasim): The person appointed to divide property among partners.
متقاسم (mutaqasim): The partner seeking division.
تمیز (tamyiz): The act of separating shares.
قبض (qabd): Taking possession of one's share.
استیفاء (istifa): Receiving one's right in full.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), on what do the partitioners testify?
A) Their own act of division.
B) The act of others, i.e., receipt and possession.
C) The value of the property.
D) The accuracy of the deed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) accepts the testimony of partitioners because they testify about the partners' receipt, not their own division.

Oath Procedure and the Critique of Accepting a Claim After Prior Affirmation
Explains the procedure of oaths and critiques accepting a claim after affirmation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for oaths when the claimant lacks evidence and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the acceptance of a claim after prior affirmation.

Core Idea
Nukūl is proof only against the refuser, but a prior affirmation does not bar a later claim of error when evidence is produced.

This lesson introduces a judicial procedure: when a claimant cannot produce evidence, partners are asked to swear oaths, and refusal (nukūl) is treated as proof against the refuser. Then we examine a subtle critique by the author of Al-Hidayah, who argues that accepting a claim after the claimant has already affirmed receipt is contradictory. Later Hanafi scholars resolve this by recognizing that the initial affirmation was based on trust, so when error is discovered, the claim can be accepted with evidence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the oath procedure
Read the opening scenario: if the claimant has no evidence, the qazi administers oaths to the partners. If any partner refuses (nukūl), that refusal is a proof against him alone, so the shares of the refuser and claimant are combined and re-proportioned.
The oath-taking partner is excluded from this re-division.
2
Grasp the principle of nukūl
Nukūl is a hujja (proof) only against the refuser, not against others. This is why only the refuser's share is affected.
3
Identify the contradiction issue
Al-Marghinani (Hidayah) objects to Quduri's ruling that a claimant who has already affirmed receipt can later bring evidence of error. He calls this a contradiction (tanāquḍ) because the claimant's prior acknowledgment contradicts his later claim.
The objection is based on the principle that a person cannot contradict his own admission.
4
Trace the dispute and resolution
Later scholars (Durr al-Mukhtar, al-Shami) counter that there is no contradiction: the claimant relied on the qasim's action when affirming; when the error becomes apparent, his prior affirmation is no longer binding because it was based on mistaken trust.
Thus, the claim can be accepted with evidence, and the division is corrected.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The later scholars' view is the relied-upon position: evidence can override the prior affirmation. This allows correction of genuine errors.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Then if evidence is not established for him, he administers an oath to the partners. So whoever among them refuses, he combines the share of the refuser and the claimant and divides between them according to their shares, because refusal is a proof only against him. So they will be treated based on their claim. Translation: So if the claimant cannot establish evidence, the qazi administers an oath to the partners (if the claimant requests). Then whoever among them refuses, he combines the shares of the refuser and the claimant and divides between them according to their shares, because refusal is a proof specifically against the refuser. So both will be dealt with according to their presumption. Its explanation has already passed in the context of the previous issue. The author of Hidayah says: the claim should not be accepted at all. He (may Allah be pleased with him) said: It is appropriate that his claim should not be accepted at all due to contradiction, and al-Quduri indicated this later. Explanation: The author of Hidayah objected to Imam Quduri's statement that after the claimant presents evidence, his statement is considered reliable. However, even after presenting evidence, his claim should not be accepted because there is conflict and contradiction in his claim. Because he previously affirmed receipt of his right, and now he claims the existence of his right, which contradicts his previous affirmation. And later, Imam Quduri stated an issue from which the same thing is derived: 'And if he says: I received up to such and such place but it was not delivered to me, and he did not testify against himself regarding receipt.' This condition 'and he did not testify' clarifies that if he had affirmed receipt, then the claim would not be accepted. I said: In Durr al-Mukhtar it is stated: There is no contradiction because he relied on the action of the ameen, then his error became apparent. And al-Shami said: The interpretation of the narrated text is that in his affirmation he relied on the action of the qasim, then when he deeply reflected, the error in his action became apparent, so he is not taken to task for that affirmation when the truth becomes apparent. From Durr al-Mukhtar vol. 5 p. 168. This statement shows there is no contradiction.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage contains two main components. First, the procedural ruling from the matn: if the claimant cannot produce evidence, the qazi administers oaths to the other partners upon the claimant's request. If a partner refuses to swear (nakala), that refusal is considered a proof against him alone, so the shares of the claimant and the refuser are combined and re-divided proportionally between them, and the oath-taking partner is excluded from this re-division. This is based on the principle that nukūl (refusal to swear) functions as a proof against the refuser only. Second, the author of Al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) critiques the earlier ruling by Quduri, arguing that even if the claimant brings evidence, his claim should not be accepted at all because it contradicts his prior affirmation of receipt. He claims Quduri himself indicated this later in the same book. The commentator then responds by citing Durr al-Mukhtar and Ibn 'Abidin (al-Shami), who argue there is no contradiction: the claimant's initial affirmation was based on his trust in the qasim's action; later the error became apparent. Therefore, his earlier acknowledgment does not prevent him from claiming the error when it becomes known. This resolution shows that the claim can be accepted if supported by evidence, despite the apparent contradiction.

Key Terms
نكول (nukūl): Refusal of a defendant to take an oath when required, which is treated as an admission against him.
تناقض (tanāquḍ): Contradiction or inconsistency in a person's statements or claims.
حجت دافعہ (hujjat dāfi'ah): A proof that repels liability; here the claimant's evidence overcomes the initial affirmation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute about accepting the claim of error after prior affirmation, what is the mufta bihi position according to the later scholars?
A) The claim is never accepted.
B) The claim is accepted only if the claimant takes an oath.
C) The claim is accepted with evidence because there is no contradiction.
D) The claim is accepted only for movable property.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows a claimant to correct a prior affirmation of receipt by bringing evidence of error, as the initial affirmation is considered conditional on the qasim's act.

Resolving Muhaya'ah Disputes and the Use of Lots
Ruling on how judge resolves dispute over spatial vs temporal allocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the procedure a Hanafi judge follows when co-owners dispute the type of muhaya'ah and explain why casting lots is used.

Core Idea
When co-owners disagree on muhaya'ah type, the judge orders agreement, then uses lots to avoid bias.

This lesson examines a procedural rule in Hanafi qada (judicial rulings) when partners dispute whether their muhaya'ah (division of usufruct) was spatial or temporal. The judge does not impose a choice because both have merits; instead he compels agreement. Once agreed on temporal, priority is determined by casting lots to eliminate partiality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Zayd claims spatial muhaya'ah (muhaya'ah fi al-makan) while Amr claims temporal (muhaya'ah fi al-zaman). Understand that each type has distinct advantages: spatial allows simultaneous use, temporal grants exclusive use of the whole property.
The judge must recognize that both types are valid but different.
2
Understand the judge's limitation
The judge cannot choose one type over the other because each is superior in different aspects: spatial is more just (simultaneous benefit), temporal offers more perfect benefit (full use during turn). Since neither is clearly preferable, the judge must order the parties to agree on one type.
Forcing agreement avoids the appearance of bias.
3
Apply the ruling upon agreement
If the parties agree on temporal muhaya'ah, the question of precedence arises: who should use the property first? The judge cannot assign priority arbitrarily.
The same logic applies: any personal choice could be seen as biased.
4
Apply qur'ah (casting lots)
To eliminate bias, the judge must cast lots between the co-owners. The one whose name is drawn gets precedence. This ensures procedural fairness and protects the judge from accusations of favoritism.
Qur'ah is a standard method in Hanafi fiqh when rights are equal and no preference exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح زید کہتا ہے کہ ہم نے مہایات فی المکان کی تھی اور عمرو کہتا ہے کہ مہایات فی الزمان ہوئی تھی اب قاضی خود سے فیصلہ نہیں کرے گا بلکہ ان دونوں کو کسی ایک پر اتفاق کا حکم کرے گا۔ کیونکہ دونوں قسمیں مختلف جہات سے ایک دوسرے سے افضل ہے تو ترجیح دشوار ہے یعنی زیادہ عدل و انصاف مہایات فی المکان میں ہے کہ دونوں بیک وقت منافع حاصل کرتے ہیں۔ اور زیادہ کمال منفعت مہایات فی الزمان میں ہے کہ پورے دار سے اپنی باری میں نفع اٹھانے کا موقع ملتا ہے تو اتفاق کا حکم ضر وری ہو گیا پھر ان دونوں نے طے کر لیا کہ مہایات فی الزمان ہو گی تو اب پہل کس سے ہو۔ تو اگر قاضی اپنے طور سے ایک کا تعین کر دے تو اس میں تہمت ہے اسلئے ان دونوں کے درمیان قرعہ ڈالا جائے اور جس کا نام نکلے اس سے پہل کر دی جائے۔
Explanation: Zayd says, 'We made a muhaya'ah in place,' and Amr says, 'The muhaya'ah was in time.' Now the judge will not decide by himself, but will order them to agree on one. Because both types are superior to each other from different aspects, so preference is difficult. That is, more justice and equity is in muhaya'ah in place because both benefit simultaneously. And more perfect benefit is in muhaya'ah in time because one gets the opportunity to benefit from the entire house during his turn. So ordering agreement became necessary. Then if they both agreed that it will be muhaya'ah in time, then who should have precedence? If the judge fixes one on his own, there is accusation of bias. Therefore, lots are cast between them, and the one whose name comes out is given precedence.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute between co-owners over the type of muhaya'ah (temporal or spatial). The judge does not choose arbitrarily; he orders them to agree. If they then agree on temporal muhaya'ah, the judge uses casting of lots to determine the order of use, avoiding any appearance of partiality.

Key Terms
مہایات فی المکان (muhaya'ah fi al-makan): Spatial division of usufruct where each co-owner uses a specific part of the property simultaneously.
قرعہ (qur'ah): A method of lottery or casting lots used to determine priority when there is no basis for preference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He orders them to agree on one type; if they agree on temporal, he uses lots for precedence.
C) He cancels the agreement and orders sale of the property.
D) He decides based on majority vote among the partners.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi judge does not impose a muhaya'ah type but compels agreement, then uses lots to determine precedence, avoiding bias.

Tahayu' on a Horse: Dispute Between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute: whether alternating use of a horse (tahayu' on manafi') is permissible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding tahayu' on the usufruct of a horse and identify the thamarah al-khilaf arising from their respective positions.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa forbids alternating use of a horse because riders' differing skills can harm the animal; the Sahibayn permit it by analogy to dividing physical objects.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on whether co-owners may alternate riding a jointly owned horse. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) permit it based on qiyas to division of physical objects. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, emphasizes the risk of harm from an unskilled rider, which would break the equality required between partners. He permits a similar arrangement for slaves because a slave can self-regulate, unlike an animal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
Recognize that the dispute is about tahayu' (alternating use) on the manafi' (usufruct) of a horse. The Sahibayn say it is permissible; Imam Abu Hanifa says it is not permissible.
The Sahibayn are Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, major students of Imam Abu Hanifa.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's qiyas
The Sahibayn draw an analogy (qiyas) to qismat a'yan (division of physical objects), where alternating possession is permissible. They argue that alternating use of usufruct is similar and therefore also permissible.
Qiyas is a source of law in Hanafi usul, but its strength depends on the illa (effective cause).
3
Examine Imam Abu Hanifa's objection
Imam Abu Hanifa argues that riders can have very different skill levels. An unskilled rider may harm the horse, thus destroying the equality that tahayu' requires. Therefore, the analogy to inanimate objects fails because animals are susceptible to damage.
Imam also permits tahayu' on a slave because a slave has free will and will not overexert himself.
4
Understand the exception for slaves
Imam distinguishes between animals and slaves: a slave can refuse to exceed his capacity, but a horse cannot resist being ridden harshly. Hence, the risk of harm is specific to animals.
This distinction shows Imam's careful consideration of the 'illa in each case.

Source Text

كتاب القسمة
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۳
اپنے اختیار سے خدمت کرتا ہے تو وہ اپنی طاقت سے زیادہ کامل نہیں کرے گا اور چو پا یہ زیادہ کامل کر لیتا ہے۔ تشریح زید اور عمر کے درمیان دو گھوڑے مشترک ہیں انہوں نے اس طرح مہایا کی ایک پر زید سوار ہوا کرے اور دوسرے پر عمر یا ایک گھوڑا، دونوں کے درمیان مشترک ہے اور انہوں نے یہ طے کیا کہ اس پر آٹھ دن زید سوار ہوا کرے اور آٹھ دن عمر تو صاحبین کے نزدیک تو یہ صورت جائز ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک جائز نہیں۔
صاحبین نے قسمت کے نزدیک تو یہ صورت جائز ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک جائز نہیں۔ صاحبین نے قسمت اعیان پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اس کو جائز کہا۔ اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک قسمت اعیان کا بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ (کما مر )

ہاں اگر یہی صورت ایک غلام اور دو غلاموں کو اندر ہو تو وہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ غلام تو صاحب اختیار ہے اپنی قدرت سے زیادہ بوجھ اٹھائے گا ہی نہیں اور چوپایہ مار پیٹ کی صورت میں اپنی طاقت سے زیادہ کا مل کر لیتا ہے اس وجہ سے دونوں کے درمیان فرق ہو گیا۔
Book of Division. Ashraf al-Bidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume 13. He serves with his choice, he will not do more than his strength, and the quadruped does more completely. Commentary: There are two horses jointly owned between Zayd and Umar. They make a tahayu' such that Zayd rides one and Umar the other, or a single horse jointly owned, and they agree that Zayd rides for eight days and Umar for eight days. According to the Sahibayn this is permissible, and according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] it is not permissible. Sahibayn, according to division [qismat], consider this permissible, and Imam also holds the same [for division of physical objects]. Also Imam's proof is that there is a difference between riders: one rider is skilled in horsemanship and will not harm the horse, the other is completely unskilled and may harm the horse. Yes, if this same case occurs with a slave and two slaves, then according to Imam it is permissible, because the slave has free will and will not carry more than his strength, whereas the quadruped may be beaten and exceed its strength; thus there is a difference between them.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of tahayu' (alternating use) of a horse based on usufruct (manafi'). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) permit it, drawing an analogy (qiyas) to the division of physical objects (qismat a'yan), which is permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, forbids it. His reasoning is that the skill levels of riders differ; one may harm the horse, destroying equality between partners. He maintains consistency by permitting the same arrangement with a slave, since a slave has free will and will not overexert himself, unlike an animal that can be forced. This shows Imam's reliance on the effective cause ('illa) of potential harm to the shared object.

Key Terms
تهايؤ (tahayu'): Mutual arrangement between co-owners to alternate use of the shared property.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, major Hanafi jurists.
قسمت اعیان (qismat a'yan): Division of physical objects themselves (as opposed to usufruct).
منافع (manafi'): Usufruct, the right to use and derive benefit from a property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because horses are too valuable
B) Because the skills of riders differ, potentially harming the horse
C) Because Sahibayn forbid it
D) Because it requires qismat a'yan

Key Takeaway
The difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on tahayu' on a horse hinges on whether qiyas on division of physical objects is valid, with Imam emphasizing the risk of harm to the animal.

Judicial and Moral Consequences When a Landowner Refuses Seeds After Plowing
Ruling on compensation for farmer when landowner refuses seeds after plowing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi judicial ruling on compensation when a landowner refuses seeds after the farmer has plowed, and explain the distinction between enforceable legal rulings and moral religious duties.

Core Idea
In court, the farmer gets no wages; but before Allah, the landowner must compensate for his deception.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in muzara'ah (sharecropping) where the landowner provides the seed but withdraws after the farmer has already plowed. The Hanafi school makes a crucial distinction between what a judge can enforce and what a person owes to Allah. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping the Hanafi approach to fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the problem
The muzara'ah contract requires the landowner to provide seed. After the farmer plows, the landowner stops. What happens to the farmer's work?
2
State the judicial ruling (hukm al-qada)
According to the text, the farmer gets nothing for his plowing in court. No wages are awarded.
This is the answer in judicial ruling (حكم قضاء).
3
Recognize the religious duty (hukm al-diyana)
Even though the court does not enforce it, the landowner has a moral/religious obligation to appease the farmer because he deceived him.
This is a duty before Allah (فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى).
4
Understand the basis: deception
The landowner's refusal after the farmer's work constitutes deception (غرور), which triggers the moral duty.
Deception is a key factor in establishing the moral obligation.
5
Apply the distinction
In any fiqh case, always distinguish between what is enforceable by a judge and what is a duty before Allah.
This dual-layer analysis is characteristic of Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عقد مزارعت طے ہو گیا اور بیج زمین والے کا تھا مگر وہ بیج ڈالنے سے رک گیا تو اسے مجبور کیا جائے گا یا نہیں۔ قال ولو امتنع رب الأرض والبذر من قبله وقد كرب المزارع الأرض فلا شيء له في عمل الكراب قيل هذا في الحكم أما فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى يلزمه استرضاء العامل لأنه غره في ذلك. ترجمہ: قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر زمین والا رک گیا اور بیج اس کی جانب سے ہے اور کاشتکار نے زمین کو جوتا ہے تو اس کو جوتنے کی مزدوری کچھ نہیں ملے گی۔ کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ جواب حکم قضاء میں ہے۔ بہر حال فيما بينه و بين الله رب الارض پر عامل کو راضی کرنا لازم ہے اس لئے کہ زمین والے نے عامل کو اس سلسلہ میں دھوکہ دیا ہے۔ تشریح: عقد مزارعت طے ہو گیا تھا اور بیج والے کا تھا مگر وہ بیج ڈالنے سے رک گیا تو حسب حکم مذکور اس کو مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا لیکن عامل نے جو کھیت جوتا ہے نالیاں وغیرہ ٹھیک کی ہیں کیا عامل کو اس کی اجرت ملے گی؟ تو فرمایا کہ نہیں یہ تو حکم قضا کا جواب ہے۔ البتہ رب الارض کا فریضہ ہوگا کہ وہ عامل کو خوش کر دے کیونکہ رب الارض نے اس کو دھوکہ دیا ہے۔
The contract of muzara'ah was finalized and the seed belonged to the landowner, but he stopped from sowing the seed; will he be compelled or not? He said: And if the landowner refrains, and the seed is from him, and the farmer has plowed the earth, then there is nothing for him for the work of plowing. It is said: This is in judicial ruling; however, between him and Allah Almighty, it is necessary for him to appease the worker because he deceived him in that. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And if the landowner stopped and the seed is from his side and the farmer has plowed the earth, then he will get nothing for the plowing. It is said that this is the answer in judicial ruling. In any case, between him and Allah, it is necessary for the landowner to appease the worker because the landowner deceived him in this matter. Explanation: The contract of muzara'ah was finalized and the seed owner stopped from sowing, so according to the mentioned ruling he will not be compelled. But the farmer plowed the field and fixed the canals etc.; will the farmer get wages for that? He said: No, this is the answer in judicial ruling. However, it is the duty of the landowner to please the farmer because the landowner deceived him.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: after a muzara'ah contract is concluded, the landowner (who provided the seed) refuses to sow the seed, but the farmer has already plowed the land. According to Hanafi fiqh, the farmer is not entitled to any wages or compensation in a court of law (hukm al-qada). However, the landowner has a moral and religious duty (fard/necessary before Allah) to appease the farmer, because his refusal after the farmer's work constitutes deception (gharar). This is based on the principle that judicial rulings follow strict legal rules, but between a person and Allah, one must act with fairness. The ruling is from Al-Quduri's matn, and the commentator explains the distinction.

Key Terms
حکم قضاء (hukm al-qada): The ruling that a judge enforces in court; based on apparent evidence.
البتہ رب الارض کا فریضہ (albattah rabb al-ard ka faridah): Moral/religious duty of the landowner to appease the farmer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a landowner refuses to provide seeds after the farmer has plowed, what is the judicial ruling regarding the farmer's claim for wages?
A) The farmer is entitled to full wages.
B) The farmer is entitled to half wages.
C) The farmer is not entitled to any wages in court.
D) The farmer is entitled to wages but must return them if the landowner objects.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the distinction between hukm al-qada and hukm al-diyana is critical: the judge cannot enforce a moral duty, but the individual must fulfill it before Allah.

Looking at a Woman's Face for Judicial Testimony
Ruling on looking at a woman's face for judicial testimony: ada vs tahammul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the ruling for looking at a woman's face during giving testimony (ada) vs bearing testimony (tahammul), and apply the Hanafi principle of necessity and intention.

Core Idea
Necessity permits looking for judicial duty, but only with proper intention and only when truly needed.

This passage from al-Quduri addresses a practical concern in Islamic courts: how a judge or witness may interact with a female party when identification is necessary. The ruling hinges on two factors: the phase of testimony (giving or bearing) and the intention of the viewer. Understanding this distinction prevents misuse while ensuring justice can be served. We will unpack the ruling, its proof from necessity, and the correct view in an intra-Hanafi difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its two contexts
The act is looking at a woman's face. It is considered in two distinct contexts: (1) when a judge or witness is giving testimony or judgment (ada), and (2) when a person is bearing testimony (tahammul) to later testify.
Ada is immediate; tahammul is for future use.
2
State the ruling for ada
For ada, it is permissible (jāʾiz) even if desire is feared, because of the necessity to uphold people's rights through judgment and testimony.
The necessity overrides the general prohibition of looking with desire.
3
Analyze the intention condition
The permissibility is conditional on the intention being for the duty (judgment/testimony), not for satisfying desire. If the intention is evil, the act becomes sinful even if outwardly valid.
Intention (qasd) is a key element in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Differentiate the ruling for tahammul
For bearing testimony, if desire is present, there is a difference of opinion. The correct view (al-aṣaḥḥ) is that it is NOT permissible, because there exists one who does not desire, so necessity is not established.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf; the text explicitly weighs the views.
5
Understand the proof (qiyas)
The ruling is based on qiyas (analogy) to the principle of necessity: when a legal duty (reviving rights) requires looking, it is permitted; when the need is not real (tahammul with desire), the prohibition remains.
The 'illa is the existence of genuine necessity (ḥāja).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی اور گواہ کیلئے عورت کا چہرے دیکھنے کا حکم
قال ويجوز للقاضي اذا ارادان يحكم عليها والشاهد اذا اراد الشهادة عليها النظر الى وجهها وان خاف ان يشتهى للحاجة الى احياء حقوق الناس بواسطة القضاء واداء الشهادة ولكن ينبغى ان يقصد به اداء الشهادة او الحكم عليها لاقضاء الشهوة تحرزا عما يمكنه التحرزعنه وهو قصد القبيح واما النظر لتحمل الشهادة اذا اشتهى قيل يباح والاصح انه لا يباح لانه يوجد من لا يشتهى فلا ضرورة بخلاف حالة الاداء.
ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور جائز ہے قاضی کیلئے جب کہ وہ ارادہ کرے کہ عورت پر فیصلہ کرے اور گواہ کے لئے جب کہ وہ عورت پر گواہی دینے کا ارادہ کرے عورت کے چہرے کی طرف دیکھنا اگر چہ شہوت کا خوف کرے فیصلہ اور اداء شہادت سے لوگوں کے حقوق کے احیاء کی جانب حاجت کی وجہ سے لیکن مناسب یہ ہے کہ اس کے ذریعہ اداء شہادت یا عورت پر فیصلہ کرنے کا ارادہ کرے نہ کہ شہوت کو پورا کرنے کا اس چیز سے بچتے ہوئے جس سے بچنا ممکن ہے اور وہ (جس سے بچنا ممکن ہے ) برائی کا قصد ہے اور بہر حال متحمل شہادت کے لئے دیکھنا جب کہ شہوت ہو کہا گیا ہے کہ مباح ہے اور اصح یہ ہے کہ مباح نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ ایسا آدمی مل سکتا ہے جس کو شہوت نہ ہو تو کوئی
Ruling for judge and witness to look at a woman's face. He (Quduri) said: It is permissible for the judge, when he intends to pass judgment on her, and for the witness, when he intends to testify regarding her, to look at her face, even if he fears desire, due to the need to revive people's rights through judgment and testimony. But he should intend thereby to give testimony or to pass judgment on her, not to satisfy desire, avoiding what he can avoid, which is the intention of evil. As for looking for the purpose of bearing testimony, if desire arises, it was said that it is permissible, but the correct view is that it is not permissible, because there exists one who does not desire, so there is no necessity, unlike the case of giving testimony. Translation: Quduri said...
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage discusses a special case: a judge or witness may look at a woman's face for judicial purposes or testimony even if desire is feared, due to the necessity of upholding people's rights. However, the intention must be proper — to fulfill the duty, not to satisfy desire. The key distinction is between giving testimony (ada) and bearing testimony (tahammul). For bearing testimony, if desire is present, the correct view is that looking is not permissible because one can find another person who does not experience desire, so there is no necessity. This is a ruling with proof from the principle of necessity and the classification of intentions.

Key Terms
اداء شہادت (ada' al-shahada): Giving testimony or presenting testimony in court.
تحمل شہادت (tahammul al-shahada): Bearing or receiving testimony, i.e., witnessing an event for future testimony.
قصد قبیح (qasd qabih): Evil intention; the intention to satisfy desire rather than fulfill a legal duty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is looking permissible for a judge even if he fears desire?
A) Because desire is always permissible in legal contexts
B) Because of the necessity to revive people's rights through judgment and testimony
C) Because looking at a woman's face is always permissible
D) Because the judge is immune to sinful desires

Key Takeaway
A judge or witness may look at a woman's face when giving testimony due to necessity, but for bearing testimony, it is not permissible if desire arises, because necessity is not established.

Looking at a Woman's Face for Judicial Purposes: Distinguishing Tahammul and Ada'
Ruling with proof: permissibility and limitations for qadi and shahid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling on looking at a woman's face for a judge or witness between the stages of bearing (tahammul) and giving (ada') testimony and apply the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Necessity permits looking for judicial purposes, but only for giving testimony, not for bearing it when desire is present.

The general prohibition of looking at non-mahram women is well-known, but the Hanafi school carves out an exception for judges and witnesses when necessary for justice. This lesson unpacks the ruling from the Hidayah commentary, distinguishing between the stage of bearing testimony (tahammul) and giving testimony (ada'). Understanding this distinction is crucial to applying the correct view in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actors and their purposes
Note who is permitted to look: the qadi (judge) and the shahid (witness). Their purposes are passing judgment and giving testimony, respectively. The ruling is specifically for those acts.
2
Note the general permissibility for judge and witness for ada'
The text states it is permissible for both to look at the woman's face even if they fear desire, due to necessity (reviving rights). The key condition is that the intention must be for the legal act, not for desire.
3
Distinguish the situation for tahammul (bearing testimony)
When a person is initially observing an incident to later testify (tahammul), the ruling differs. If he fears desire, the correct view (al-asahh) is that looking is not permissible, because another witness without desire can be found.
4
Understand the reasoning: necessity and availability of alternatives
For ada', the witness is already committed and no substitute is available, so necessity overrides the prohibition. For tahammul, a substitute can be sought, so no necessity exists. The ruling is based on the principle of necessity (darura) and the availability of alternatives.
This is an application of istihsan (juristic preference).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجوز للقاضي اذا ارادان يحكم عليها والشاهد اذا اراد الشهادة عليها النظر الى وجهها وان خاف ان يشتهى للحاجة الى احياء حقوق الناس بواسطة القضاء واداء الشهادة ولكن ينبغى ان يقصد به اداء الشهادة او الحكم عليها لاقضاء الشهوة تحرزا عما يمكنه التحرزعنه وهو قصد القبيح واما النظر لتحمل الشهادة اذا اشتهى قيل يباح والاصح انه لا يباح لانه يوجد من لا يشتهى فلا ضرورة بخلاف حالة الاداء.
ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور جائز ہے قاضی کیلئے جب کہ وہ ارادہ کرے کہ عورت پر فیصلہ کرے اور گواہ کے لئے جب کہ وہ عورت پر گواہی دینے کا ارادہ کرے عورت کے چہرے کی طرف دیکھنا اگر چہ شہوت کا خوف کرے فیصلہ اور اداء شہادت سے لوگوں کے حقوق کے احیاء کی جانب حاجت کی وجہ سے لیکن مناسب یہ ہے کہ اس کے ذریعہ اداء شہادت یا عورت پر فیصلہ کرنے کا ارادہ کرے نہ کہ شہوت کو پورا کرنے کا اس چیز سے بچتے ہوئے جس سے بچنا ممکن ہے اور وہ (جس سے بچنا ممکن ہے ) برائی کا قصد ہے اور بہر حال متحمل شہادت کے لئے دیکھنا جب کہ شہوت ہو کہا گیا ہے کہ مباح ہے اور اصح یہ ہے کہ مباح نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ ایسا آدمی مل سکتا ہے جس کو شہوت نہ ہو تو کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے بخلاف ادائیگی کی حالت کے۔
تشریح قاضی اور گواہ کو فیصلہ اور اداء شہادت کے لئے عورت کا چہرہ دیکھنا جائز ہے اگر چہ شہوت کا خوف ہو تب بھی ، کیوں کہ اگر وہ خوف شہادت کی وجہ سے دیکھنے سے رکیں گے تو فیصلہ کیسے کرے گا اور شہادت کیسے دے گا تو فیصلہ اور اداء شہادت کا دروازہ بند ہو جائے گا جس سے لوگوں کے حقوق پامال ہوں گے ، اور ضرورت احیاء حقوق ناس کی ہے تو دیکھنا جائز ہوا لیکن یہ دونوں قضاء شہوت کا قصد نہ کریں بلکہ فیصلہ اور اداء شہادت کا قصد کریں کیونکہ نیت تو درست کی جاسکتی ہے لہذا جس چیز سے بچنا ممکن ہے اس سے بچنا ضروری ہوگا اور قصد نیچ سے بچنا ممکن ہے۔
پھر ایک تو شہادت کا متحمل ہے اور ایک اداء ہے اگر ادائے گی کے وقت شہوت ہو تب بھی وہ شہادت دے گا اور دیکھنا جائز ہوگا کیوں کہ یہاں ادائیگی کے لئے یہی متعین ہے کیوں کہ تمل شہادت اس نے کیا تھا تو یہ عذر ہے اور اگر بوقت متحمل شہادت شہوت ہو تو وہاں دیکھنا کیسا ہے تو اس میں دو قول ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ دیکھنا جائز ہے اور دوسرا قول جو اصح ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ دیکھنا جائز نہیں ہے کیوں کہ ایسا آدمی مل سکتا ہے جو قتل شہادت کرے اور اس میں شہوت نہ ہو، در مختارص ۲۳۷ ج ۵ پر بھی یہی مذکور ہے کہ شہوت وقت تحمل شہادت میں دیکھنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
تنبیہ قاضی کو فیصلہ کرنے کے لئے عورت کے جانے کی ضرورت ہے تا کہ مجہول پر فیصلہ نہ ہو اور اسی طرح تحمل شہادت بغیر دیکھے جائز نہیں ہے البتہ اگر شاہد نے عورت کی آواز سن لی اور جو عورتیں اس کے پاس ہیں انہوں نے خبر دیدی کہ یہ فلاں بول رہی ہے اور شاہد کو اس پر اعتماد ہو گیا تو اس کو گواہی دینا جائز ہے وہو المختار کذافی سکب الانہر برص ۴۶۶ ج ۲
[Al-Quduri] said: And it is permissible for the judge, when he intends to pass a judgment against her, and for the witness, when he intends to give testimony against her, to look at her face, even if he fears he may desire her, due to the need to revive people's rights through judgment and testimony. But it is appropriate that he intends thereby to give testimony or to pass judgment, not to fulfill desire, avoiding what he can avoid, that is, the intention of evil. As for looking for the purpose of bearing testimony (tahammul al-shahada) when he desires, it is said to be permissible, but the correct view is that it is not permissible, because there may be found someone who does not desire, so there is no necessity, unlike the situation of giving testimony (ada'). Translation: Al-Quduri said: And it is permissible for the judge, when he intends to give a ruling against her, and for the witness, when he intends to give testimony against her, to look at her face, even if he fears desire, due to the need to revive people's rights through judgment and testimony. But it is appropriate that he intends thereby to give testimony or to pass judgment, not to fulfill desire, avoiding what he can avoid, and that (what he can avoid) is the intention of evil. And as for looking for bearing testimony when there is desire, it is said to be permissible, but the correct view is that it is not permissible, because there may be found someone who does not desire, so there is no necessity, unlike the situation of giving testimony. Explanation: It is permissible for the judge and witness to look at a woman's face for judgment and testimony, even if there is fear of desire, because if they refrain from looking due to that fear, how will they judge and how will they testify? Then the door of judgment and testimony would close, leading to the loss of people's rights. And the necessity of reviving rights is present, so looking is permissible. But both should not intend fulfilling desire; rather, they should intend judgment and testimony, because the intention can be corrected. Therefore, one must avoid what is possible to avoid, and avoiding evil intention is possible. Then, one is a bearer of testimony (mutahammil) and one is a giver of testimony (mu'addi). If at the time of giving testimony there is desire, he will still give testimony and looking is permissible, because here he is specifically assigned to give testimony, as he had already borne the testimony, so this is an excuse. As for looking at the time of bearing testimony when there is desire, there are two views: one says it is permissible, and the second, which is correct, says it is not permissible, because there can be found a person who does not desire, so there is no necessity. In Durr Mukhtar, vol. 5, p. 237, it is also mentioned that looking at the time of bearing testimony with desire is not permissible. Note: The judge needs to know the woman (i.e., see her) to pass judgment so that he does not judge an unknown person. Similarly, bearing testimony without seeing is not permissible. However, if the witness heard the woman's voice and the women with her informed him that she is saying such-and-such, and he becomes confident, then giving testimony is permissible. This is the chosen view, as in Sabk al-Anhar, vol. 2, p. 466.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility for a judge (qadi) or witness (shahid) to look at a woman's face during legal proceedings. The general rule is that looking at a non-mahram woman with desire is prohibited, but necessity permits it here. The judge and witness need to see the woman to identify her and to ensure justice. The ruling distinguishes between two stages: bearing testimony (tahammul) and giving testimony (ada'). For giving testimony, looking is permissible even if desire is present, because the witness is already assigned and must fulfill his duty. For bearing testimony, the correct view is that looking is not permissible if desire is present, because another person without desire could be found. The key is that the intention must be for the legal purpose, not for desire. This is a practical application of istihsan (juristic preference) based on the need to protect people's rights.

Key Terms
قاضی (qadi): A judge who passes legal judgments; here specifically looking at a woman for passing judgment.
شاہد (shahid): A witness who gives testimony; here distinguishing between bearing (tahammul) and giving (ada') testimony.
تحمل شہادت (tahammul al-shahada): The process of receiving or bearing testimony, i.e., hearing and observing an incident to later testify.
اداء شہادت (ada' al-shahada): The act of giving or delivering testimony in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi view, when is it permissible for a witness to look at a woman's face if he fears desire?
A) Only when bearing testimony (tahammul).
B) Only when giving testimony (ada') in court.
C) At both stages if he intends justice.
D) Never, because desire invalidates the act.

Key Takeaway
Necessity permits a qadi or shahid to look at a woman's face for judicial purposes during ada', but not during tahammul if desire is present, because an alternative witness can be found.

The Qadi's Procedure Against Hoarding
Procedure for qadi to handle hoarding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the graduated procedure a qadi follows when a hoarding case is brought before him.

Core Idea
The qadi first warns, then punishes — a graduated enforcement against hoarding.

This lesson outlines the legal steps a qadi must take when a complaint of hoarding (ihtikar) is presented. The procedure prioritizes warning and compliance before resorting to punitive measures, reflecting the Hanafi principle of gradation in enforcement. You will learn the two-stage process that balances public welfare with the rights of the hoarder.

Guided Path
1
Identify the complaint and the qadi's first action
The qadi first orders the muhtakir (hoarder) to sell what is surplus to his own and his family's needs, and forbids him from hoarding. This is the initial, non-punitive step.
The order includes an allowance for ease (bi i'tibar al-sa'ah), meaning the hoarder is not forced to sell in hardship.
2
Recognize the condition for punishment
The qadi only proceeds to punishment if the matter is brought to him a second time, indicating that the hoarder has not complied with the first order.
This ensures a warning is given before punitive measures are taken.
3
State the punishment and its purpose
Upon repeat violation, the qadi may imprison the hoarder and administer ta'zir (discretionary punishment) as he sees fit, with the purpose of deterrence and preventing harm to the public.
Ta'zir is adaptive; the qadi decides the severity based on the situation.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage outlines the legal procedure when a case of ihtikar is brought before the qadi. The qadi first orders the hoarder to sell the surplus grain beyond what is needed for himself and his family, taking into account a reasonable standard of living. He also warns him against hoarding. If the hoarder repeats the offense, the qadi may imprison him and impose discretionary punishment (ta'zir) as a deterrent and to protect the public from harm. This ruling is based on the principle of preventing harm (darar) and is a practical enforcement mechanism for the prohibition of ihtikar.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment determined by the qadi for offenses that have no fixed hadd penalty.
احتكار (ihtikar): Hoarding essential goods (especially foodstuffs) to create scarcity and drive up prices, which is prohibited in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Judge's Two-Step Procedure for Hoarding Complaint
Judge's procedure against hoarder

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two-step procedure a Hanafi judge follows when a hoarding complaint is brought and apply it to a modern economic scenario.

Core Idea
A judge first orders sale of surplus; only on repeat offense does he punish.

This passage from Al-Hidayah details the graded response a judge must take when a hoarding complaint reaches him. It distinguishes between the initial advice and the subsequent punitive measures, reflecting the Hanafi emphasis on gradual correction and public welfare.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first action upon first complaint
The judge orders the hoarder to sell what exceeds the needs of himself and his family, considering ease, and forbids him from hoarding. No punishment is imposed initially.
The condition 'considering ease' means the hoarder is allowed a reasonable amount for his own consumption.
2
Recognize the condition for punishment
Punishment (imprisonment and ta'zir) only occurs if the hoarder repeats the offense after the first warning. The judge determines the severity of ta'zir based on what deters and removes public harm.
Ta'zir is discretionary, as per Hanafi fiqh.
3
Understand the underlying rationale
The procedure aims to prevent harm (darar) to the public. The first step is educative; the second is punitive to ensure compliance.
This reflects the maxim 'Harm must be removed' (al-darar yuzal).
