When Price Fixing (Tas'ir) Becomes Permissible for the Judge
Sets condition for price fixing: when sellers transgress excessively and judge cannot protect rights otherwise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions under which a Hanafi judge may fix prices and explain why the default prohibition is lifted.

Core Idea
Price fixing is prohibited in principle, but becomes permissible when sellers grossly overcharge and the judge has no other way to protect rights.

We begin with the general Hanafi position that price fixing (tas'ir) is prohibited as it interferes with free market transactions. However, the jurists recognized an exception: when sellers become oppressive and the public interest cannot be safeguarded otherwise. This passage from the Hidayah clarifies the precise conditions that justify intervention by the judge, emphasizing the role of expert consultation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling on price fixing
Recall that the Hanafi school generally prohibits price fixing (tas'ir) because it restricts the freedom of sellers. This passage builds on that by defining an exception.
The default ruling is haram/prohibited.
2
Locate the first condition: gross transgression by sellers
The passage states that sellers must 'transgress against the value with gross transgression' (tajawuz fahish). This means overcharging far beyond the fair market price, not mere increase.
Minor overcharging does not trigger this exception.
3
Locate the second condition: inability to protect rights otherwise
The judge must be 'incapable of safeguarding the rights of Muslims except by price fixing.' This means all other measures (admonition, mediation, etc.) have failed or are ineffective.
If other means work, price fixing remains prohibited.
4
Note the procedural requirement: consultation with experts
The judge must fix prices 'with the consultation of people of opinion and insight' (ahl al-ray wa al-basirah). These are knowledgeable market experts who understand fair pricing.
The judge cannot fix prices arbitrarily.
5
Understand the legal rationale: repelling harm
The underlying principle is the removal of hardship (raf' al-haraj) and prevention of oppression (zulm). When sellers' transgression causes widespread harm, price fixing becomes a necessary tool to protect the community.
This balances the prohibition against the public good.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی کب بھاؤ مقرر کر سکتا ہے
فان كان ارباب الطعام يتحكمون ويتعدون عن القيمة تعديا فاحشا وعجز القاضي عن صيانة حقوق المسلمين الا بالتسعيــر فـحـيـنـتـذ لا بأس به بمشورة من اهل الراى والبصيرة
ترجمہ. پس اگر ہوں غلہ والے تحکم کرتے ہوں اور تجاوز کرتے ہوں قیمت سے تجاوز فاحش اور قاضی عاجز ہو جائے مسلمانوں کے حقوق کی حفاظت سے مگر بھاؤ مقرر کرنے کے ساتھ ، تو اس وقت بھاؤ مقرر کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں اہل رائے اور اہل بصیرت کے مشورہ سے۔
تشریح جولوگ غلہ فروش ہیں جیسے ہمارے یہاں پیسے جو لوگوں پر ظلم و ستم کرنے پر کمر بستہ ہیں اور بغیر کنٹرول ریٹ کے لوگوں کے حقوق کی حفاظت مشکل ہے تو اس وقت کنٹرول ریٹ مقرر کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں بلکہ قاضی ایسا کر دے تا کہ لوگ ظلم وستم سے محفوظ رہ سکیں لیکن قاضی کو چاہئے کہ ہر زمانہ میں باشعور لوگوں سے مشورہ کرے کہ کیا ریٹ مقرر کیا جائے جن کو غلہ کے معاملہ میں تجربہ اور شعور ہوتا که فریقین نقصان اور خسارہ سے محفوظ رہ سکیں۔
When can the judge fix prices? So if the owners of grain act arbitrarily and transgress against the value with gross transgression, and the judge is incapable of safeguarding the rights of Muslims except by price fixing, then at that time there is no harm in it, with the consultation of people of opinion and insight. Translation: If the grain sellers act despotically and exceed the price excessively, and the judge is unable to protect the rights of Muslims except by fixing prices, then at that time there is no harm in fixing prices, with consultation of people of opinion and insight. Explanation: Those who are grain sellers, like here [some] are intent on oppressing people, and without control rates protecting people's rights is difficult, then at that time there is no harm in fixing control rates; rather the judge should do so to protect people from oppression. But the judge must consult sensible people at every time to decide what rate to fix, so that both parties are protected from loss and damage.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage explains the condition under which the judge may legitimately fix prices. It builds on the earlier general prohibition by specifying that if grain sellers become tyrannical and grossly overcharge (fuhsh al-taghyir), and the judge has no other means to protect the Muslims' rights, then price fixing becomes permissible. This is conditional upon consultation with knowledgeable and insightful people (ahl al-ray wa al-basirah) to determine a fair price. The commentary stresses that the judge should not act alone but seek expert advice to ensure justice for both buyers and sellers. This is a clear application of the principle of repelling harm (darar).

Key Terms
تجاوز فاحش (tajawuz fahish): Gross transgression or excessive overcharging beyond the fair market value.
تسعیر (tas'ir): The act of fixing prices by a public authority (judge, ruler, etc.).
أهل الرأي والبصيرة (ahl al-ray wa al-basirah): People of opinion and insight; knowledgeable experts in the market who can determine fair prices.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Any complaint from the public
B) The sellers exceed the price excessively and the judge cannot protect rights otherwise
C) The sellers are rich
D) The judge has authority from the ruler

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi judge may fix prices only when sellers grossly overcharge (tajawuz fahish) and he has no other means to protect rights, and even then only with expert consultation.

Sale Above Fixed Price: Validity Despite Violation
Ruling on validity of sale exceeding judicially fixed price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale above the judge's fixed price and explain why the sale is valid despite the violation.

Core Idea
A sale above the fixed price is valid but sinful because a free person is not under interdiction.

When a judge fixes prices and a seller disobeys by selling at a higher amount, the Hanafi school does not invalidate the transaction. This lesson explains the principle of no hajr (interdiction) on a free adult, which forms the basis for this ruling, and the exceptions recognised by the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling goods above the price fixed by the judge. The ruling is that the sale is valid (sahih) but the seller commits a sin.
The text says 'ajaza al-qadi' – the judge validates the sale, meaning he does not annul it.
2
Locate the basis in Abu Hanifa's principle
Abu Hanifa does not allow hajr (interdiction) on a free person regarding his property. Since the seller is free and not forced, the contract stands.
Hajr would restrict the right to sell; its absence means the sale is effective.
3
Note the agreement of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani agree with Abu Hanifa, except if the judge placed interdiction on a specific group (e.g., debtors). Then a sale above the fixed price might be invalid.
The exception shows that hajr can be placed on specific individuals for a valid reason.
4
Understand the condition of free choice
The seller is not forced (ghayr mukrah) to sell; he chooses to sell at a higher price. That lack of coercion makes the contract voluntary and valid.
If the seller were coerced, the sale might be fasid (voidable).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جو قاضی کی حکم عدولی کرے اس کیلئے کیا حکم ہے
فاذا فعل ذالك وتعدى رجل عن ذلك وباع باكثر منه اجازة القاضي وهذا ظاهر عند لهى حنيفة لانه لا يرى الحجر على الحروكذا عندهما الا ان يكون الحجر على قوم باعيانهم ومن باع منهم بما قدره الامام صح لانه غير مكره على البيع وهل يبيع القاضى عن المحتكر طعامه من غير رضاه قيل هو على الاختلاف الذى عرف فى بيع مال المديون وقيل يبيع بالاتفاق لان ابا حنيفة يرى الحجر لدفع ضرر عام وهذا كذالك
ترجمہ. پس اگر قاضی نے ایسا کر دیا ( کنٹرول ریٹ مقرر کر دیا ) اور کسی شخص نے اس سے تجاوز کیا اور اس سے زیادہ کے ساتھ فروخت کر دیا تو اس قاضی اس بیع کو جائز قرار دے گا (یعنی اس کو توڑے گا نہیں) اور یہ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تو ظاہر ہے اسلئے کہ وہ آزاد پر حجر کو جائز نہیں سمجھتے اور اسی طرح صاحبین کے نزدیک بھی (ظاہر ہے) مگر یہ کہ حجر کسی معین جماعت پر ہو ؟ اور جس نے ان میں سے بیچا اس کے مقرر کردہ قیمت پر تو وہ بیع صحیح ہے اسلئے کہ وہ بیچنے پر مجبور نہیں اور کیا قاضی محتکر کا غلہ اس کی رضا مندی کے بغیر بیچ سکتا ہے؟ کہا گیا ہے کہ وہ اس اختلاف پر ہے جو قرضدار کے مال کی بیع میں معروف ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ اتفاق سے بیچ سکتا ہے اسلئے کہ ابو حنیفہ عام ضرر کو دور کرنے کے لئے حجر کو جائز سمجھتے ہیں اور یہ بھی ایسا ہی ہے۔
What is the ruling for one who disobeys the judge? So when he has done that (fixed prices) and a man transgresses against that and sells for more than it, the judge validates the sale. This is apparent according to Abu Hanifa, because he does not consider placing interdiction (hajr) on a free person, and likewise in the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), except if the interdiction is on a specific group of people. And whoever among them sells at the price set by the ruler, it is valid because he is not forced to sell. And can the judge sell the hoarder's food without his consent? It is said it is upon the difference known in the sale of the property of a debtor. And it is said that he can sell by agreement, because Abu Hanifa considers interdiction permissible to repel general harm, and this is similar. Translation: If the judge has done that (fixed control rates) and a person transgresses and sells for more, the judge validates the sale. This is apparent according to Abu Hanifa because he does not allow interdiction on a free person, and similarly according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), except if the interdiction is on a specific group. And whoever among them sells at the price fixed by the ruler, the sale is valid because he is not forced to sell. And can the judge sell the hoarder's food without his consent? It is said that it is upon the difference known in the sale of a debtor's property, and it is said that he can sell by agreement, because Abu Hanifa considers interdiction permissible to repel general harm, and this is similar.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues. First, if a person disobeys the judge's price fixing and sells for more, the judge does not invalidate the sale; rather he validates it because, according to Abu Hanifa, placing interdiction (hajr) on a free person is not allowed—the seller is not forced, so the contract is valid even if it violates the price regulation. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree except concerning a specific group under interdiction. Second, there is a question: can the judge sell the hoarder's food without his consent? There are two opinions: one refers to the difference of opinion in the sale of a debtor's property (whether the judge can sell without consent); the other says the judge can sell by agreement because Abu Hanifa permits interdiction to repel general harm, and hoarding causes general harm. The passage ends with the statement that this is similar, indicating endorsement of forced sale.

Key Terms
حجر (hajr): Interdiction or restriction on a person's ability to dispose of property. In this lesson, it refers to prohibiting a free person from selling at any price.
إجازة القاضي (ijāzat al-qāḍī): The judge validates the transaction; he does not annul it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the price control is not binding in Hanafi fiqh

Key Takeaway
A sale above the judge's fixed price is valid because a free person is not subject to hajr, but the seller commits a sin by disobeying the order.

Forced Sale of Hoarder's Food Without Consent: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on forced sale of hoarder's goods without consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two opinions within the Hanafi school regarding forced sale of a hoarder's food without his consent and explain the preferred view based on preventing general harm.

Core Idea
The judge may sell the hoarder's food without consent because preventing general harm justifies interdiction.

Hoarders cause public harm by withholding food. The Hanafi school debates whether the judge can sell such food without the hoarder's consent. Two views emerge: one refers to the ikhtilaf in selling a debtor's property, while the other allows it by agreement based on Abu Hanifa's principle of repelling general harm. This lesson analyses both positions and the reasoning behind the preferred ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
The question: Can the judge sell the hoarder's food without his consent?
Hoarder (muhtakir) withholds goods to drive up prices.
2
State the first opinion
First opinion: The ruling is subject to the same difference of opinion (ikhtilaf) as the sale of a debtor's property (whether the judge can sell without consent).
In that precedent, some Hanafis allowed it, others required consent.
3
State the second opinion
Second opinion: The judge can sell by agreement (bil-ittifāq) because Abu Hanifa permits hajr to repel general harm, and hoarding causes general harm.
This opinion is attributed to Abu Hanifa's broader principle.
4
Determine the preferred view
The text ends with 'and this is similar', indicating endorsement of the second opinion: forced sale is allowed to prevent public harm.
This is consistent with the purpose of Islamic law to prevent harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جو قاضی کی حکم عدولی کرے اس کیلئے کیا حکم ہے
فاذا فعل ذالك وتعدى رجل عن ذلك وباع باكثر منه اجازة القاضي وهذا ظاهر عند لهى حنيفة لانه لا يرى الحجر على الحروكذا عندهما الا ان يكون الحجر على قوم باعيانهم ومن باع منهم بما قدره الامام صح لانه غير مكره على البيع وهل يبيع القاضى عن المحتكر طعامه من غير رضاه قيل هو على الاختلاف الذى عرف فى بيع مال المديون وقيل يبيع بالاتفاق لان ابا حنيفة يرى الحجر لدفع ضرر عام وهذا كذالك
ترجمہ. پس اگر قاضی نے ایسا کر دیا ( کنٹرول ریٹ مقرر کر دیا ) اور کسی شخص نے اس سے تجاوز کیا اور اس سے زیادہ کے ساتھ فروخت کر دیا تو اس قاضی اس بیع کو جائز قرار دے گا (یعنی اس کو توڑے گا نہیں) اور یہ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تو ظاہر ہے اسلئے کہ وہ آزاد پر حجر کو جائز نہیں سمجھتے اور اسی طرح صاحبین کے نزدیک بھی (ظاہر ہے) مگر یہ کہ حجر کسی معین جماعت پر ہو ؟ اور جس نے ان میں سے بیچا اس کے مقرر کردہ قیمت پر تو وہ بیع صحیح ہے اسلئے کہ وہ بیچنے پر مجبور نہیں اور کیا قاضی محتکر کا غلہ اس کی رضا مندی کے بغیر بیچ سکتا ہے؟ کہا گیا ہے کہ وہ اس اختلاف پر ہے جو قرضدار کے مال کی بیع میں معروف ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ اتفاق سے بیچ سکتا ہے اسلئے کہ ابو حنیفہ عام ضرر کو دور کرنے کے لئے حجر کو جائز سمجھتے ہیں اور یہ بھی ایسا ہی ہے۔
What is the ruling for one who disobeys the judge? So when he has done that (fixed prices) and a man transgresses against that and sells for more than it, the judge validates the sale. This is apparent according to Abu Hanifa, because he does not consider placing interdiction (hajr) on a free person, and likewise in the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), except if the interdiction is on a specific group of people. And whoever among them sells at the price set by the ruler, it is valid because he is not forced to sell. And can the judge sell the hoarder's food without his consent? It is said it is upon the difference known in the sale of the property of a debtor. And it is said that he can sell by agreement, because Abu Hanifa considers interdiction permissible to repel general harm, and this is similar. Translation: If the judge has done that (fixed control rates) and a person transgresses and sells for more, the judge validates the sale. This is apparent according to Abu Hanifa because he does not allow interdiction on a free person, and similarly according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), except if the interdiction is on a specific group. And whoever among them sells at the price fixed by the ruler, the sale is valid because he is not forced to sell. And can the judge sell the hoarder's food without his consent? It is said that it is upon the difference known in the sale of a debtor's property, and it is said that he can sell by agreement, because Abu Hanifa considers interdiction permissible to repel general harm, and this is similar.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues. First, if a person disobeys the judge's price fixing and sells for more, the judge does not invalidate the sale; rather he validates it because, according to Abu Hanifa, placing interdiction (hajr) on a free person is not allowed—the seller is not forced, so the contract is valid even if it violates the price regulation. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree except concerning a specific group under interdiction. Second, there is a question: can the judge sell the hoarder's food without his consent? There are two opinions: one refers to the difference of opinion in the sale of a debtor's property (whether the judge can sell without consent); the other says the judge can sell by agreement because Abu Hanifa permits interdiction to repel general harm, and hoarding causes general harm. The passage ends with the statement that this is similar, indicating endorsement of forced sale.

Key Terms
محتکر (muhtakir): A hoarder who withholds essential goods to cause scarcity and raise prices.
ضرر عام (ḍarar ʿāmm): General harm that affects the public welfare.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the preferred view that the judge may sell the hoarder's food without consent?
A) The judge has absolute authority over all property
B) Abu Hanifa allows hajr to repel general harm
C) The hoarder loses property rights by hoarding
D) The buyer has a right to purchase at any price

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, through Abu Hanifa's principle of repelling general harm, permits the judge to sell a hoarder's food without consent, with the preferred view allowing it to protect the public.

Ruling on a Qadi's Salary: Permissible with Conditions
Ruling on qadi's salary with proofs from Sunnah and qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a qadi's salary, identify the proofs, and distinguish between permissible and prohibited scenarios based on the condition of stipulation.

Core Idea
A qadi may receive a salary from the treasury, but stipulating it as a condition makes it haram.

In this passage from the Hidayah, Imam Muhammad addresses a critical question: can a qadi (judge) receive a salary from the public treasury? The answer is nuanced—permissible under certain conditions, but prohibited if stipulated. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proofs from the Sunnah and analogy, and the underlying rationale to prevent confusion with bribery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is a qadi taking a salary (rizq) from the treasury. Determine the default hukm level (mubah) and the exception (haram when stipulated).
The ruling has two parts: default permissibility and conditional prohibition.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
What proof does the author cite? The Prophet (peace be upon him) assigned stipends to 'Attab ibn Usayd and 'Ali (radhiyallahu anhuma). This is a direct Sunnah evidence.
Also mentions qiyas (analogy) to the executor (wasi) and mudarib.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal reasoning)
How does the proof prove permissibility? The Prophet's action of assigning a stipend indicates permissibility. The qiyas establishes that confinement for the rights of Muslims entitles one to maintenance from their wealth.
The illa (effective cause) is 'confinement for benefit of others'.
4
Identify the conditions
What are the conditions for permissibility? The salary must be sufficient (kifayah) and not stipulated as a condition of appointment. If stipulated, it becomes ijarah 'ala al-ta'ah (hiring for worship), which is haram.
Stipulation changes the nature of the payment from permissible gift to prohibited wage.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Given the conditions, what is the mufta bihi? The qadi may accept a salary if it is given without stipulation, but he must not demand it. The ruler should provide it from the treasury as a necessity.
This prevents conflicts of interest and preserves the integrity of the judiciary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا باس برزق القاضى لانه عليه السلام بعث عتاب بن اسيد الى مكة وفرض له وبعث عليا الى اليمن وفرض له ولا نه محبوس لحق المسلمين فتكون نفقته فى مالهم وهو مال بيت المال وهذا لان الحبس من اسباب النفقة كما فى الوصى والمضارب اذا سافر بمال المضاربة وهذا فيمايكون كفاية فان كان شرطا فهو حرام لانه استیجار على الطاعة اذا القضاء طاعة بل هو افضلها ترجمہ امام محمد نے فرمایا اور قاضی کے رزق میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے عتاب بن اسید رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کو مکہ کی طرف بھیجا اور ان کیلئے نفقہ مقررفرمایا اور حضرت علی کو یمن کی جانب بھیجا اور ان کیلئے نفقہ مقرر فرمایا اور اسلئے کہ قاضی حق مسلمین میں محبوس ہے تو ہوگا اس کا نفقہ مسلمانوں کے مال میں۔ اور وہ بیت المال کا مال ہے اور یہ اسلئے کہ جس نفقہ کے اسباب میں سے ہے۔ جیسا کہ وصی اور مضارب میں جبکہ مضارب مال مضاربت کے ساتھ سفر کر ہے اور یہ جواز اس مقدار میں ہے جو بقدر کفایت ہو۔ پس اگر شرط ہو تو یہ حرام ہے اسلئے کہ طاعت پر اجرت لینا ہے اسلئے کہ قضاء طاعت بلکہ افضل طاعت ہے۔ تشریح امیر المومنین قاضی کا رزق بیت المال سے دے اور قاضی کے لینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کیونکہ خود آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے عتاب بن اسید کو مکہ کا اور حضرت علی گویمن کا عامل مقر فرمایا اور ان کیلئے نفقہ مقرر فرمایا اور اس زمانہ میں بیت المال نہیں تھا تو آنحضرت اپنے مال سے دیا کرتے تھے (وفیہ تفصیل) اور چونکہ قاضی مسلمانوں کے امور کیلئے محبوس ہے تو ان کا نفقہ بھی مسلمانوں کے مال میں سے ملنا چاہئے اور مسلمانوں کا مال بیت المال کا مال ہے کیونکہ کسی کیلئے محبوس ہونا اسباب نفقہ میں سے ہے جیسے وصی جبکہ وہ یتیم کے کام میں پھنسا ر ہے تو اس کے مال میں سے اپنا نفقه بقدر کفایت لینا جائز ہے اور ایسے ہی مضارب جبکہ وہ مال مضاربت کو لے کر سفر کرے اسی میں سے بقدر کفایت اپنا نفقہ لے سکتا ہے۔
He said: There is no harm in the qadi's salary (rizq) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) sent 'Attab ibn Usayd to Mecca and assigned a stipend for him, and sent 'Ali to Yemen and assigned a stipend for him. And because the qadi is confined for the rights of the Muslims, so his expenditure should be from their wealth, which is the wealth of the treasury (bayt al-mal). This is because confinement is one of the causes of maintenance, as in the case of the executor (wasi) and the mudarib when he travels with the mudaraba capital. This is to the extent of sufficiency. If it is stipulated (as a condition), then it is haram because it is hiring for an act of obedience, since adjudication is an act of obedience, indeed the best of acts of obedience. Commentary: The leader should give the qadi his salary from the treasury, and there is no harm in the qadi taking it. This is proven by the Prophet's practice of assigning stipends to his governors. Since the qadi is confined for the affairs of the Muslims, his maintenance is from the Muslims' wealth, i.e., the treasury. Being confined is a cause for maintenance, similar to an executor who is busy with the orphan's estate—he may take a reasonable maintenance from it—and a mudarib traveling with the capital.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs regarding the permissibility of a qadi receiving a salary (rizq) from the public treasury (bayt al-mal). Imam Muhammad states there is no harm, based on the prophetic practice of assigning stipends to officials like 'Attab ibn Usayd and 'Ali. The legal reason (illa) is that the qadi is confined (mahbus) for the Muslims' rights, so his upkeep should be from their wealth, analogous to an executor (wasi) and a mudarib who may take maintenance when engaged in their duties. However, the permission is conditional: the salary must be sufficient (kifayah) and not stipulated as a condition of the appointment. If the qadi stipulates a salary as a condition, it becomes haram because it would constitute hiring for an act of obedience (ijarah 'ala al-ta'ah), which is prohibited as acts of worship should be done for Allah alone. The Urdu commentary clarifies that the Prophet used to give from his own wealth before the establishment of the treasury. The analogy with the wasi and mudarib illustrates that confinement for another's benefit entitles one to basic maintenance.

Key Terms
رزق القاضي (rizq al-qāḍī): Salary or stipend given to a judge from the public treasury.
بيت المال (bayt al-māl): The public treasury of the Muslims.
حبس (ḥabs): Confinement or being occupied for a specific purpose, here for the rights of Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a qadi's salary become haram according to the passage?
A) When it is taken from the treasury
B) When it is stipulated as a condition of appointment
C) When it is more than sufficiency
D) When the qadi does not need it

Key Takeaway
A qadi may receive a salary from the treasury without stipulation, but stipulating it as a condition makes it prohibited (haram).

Judge's Salary: Permissibility, Obligation, and Prohibition
Ruling with proof on judge's salary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge's salary, distinguish when it is permissible, wajib, or haram, and apply the condition of prior stipulation.

Core Idea
A judge's salary is permissible if not stipulated, but becomes haram if conditioned; obligatory for the poor, preferable for the wealthy.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the delicate balance between public treasury rights and judicial integrity. It establishes that a judge may receive a salary from Bayt al-Mal, but the permissibility is not absolute—it hinges on whether the salary was stipulated in advance and on the judge's financial status. The Hanafi school navigates this with proofs from the Prophet's practice and qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State the default ruling for a judge taking salary without any condition. According to Imam Muhammad, 'there is no harm' (la ba'sa). This is mubah (permissible).
2
Examine the proofs
The first proof is the Prophet's practice: he sent 'Attab ibn Asid to Mecca and 'Ali to Yemen and fixed stipends for them. The second is qiyas: the judge is occupied for Muslims' rights, similar to an executor (wasi) or a mudarib who may take expenses from trust property.
These are dalil naqli and qiyas respectively.
3
Understand the prohibition when stipulated
If the salary is made a condition of appointment, it becomes haram because it is hiring for an act of worship (ijarah 'ala al-ta'ah). Judgment is the best of worship.
This condition turns the salary into a contractual obligation, which is not allowed.
4
Differentiate poor vs wealthy judge
For a poor judge, taking the salary is not just permissible but obligatory (wajib) because he cannot fulfill the duty of judgment otherwise. For a wealthy judge, there are two views: abstinence is better to preserve Bayt al-Mal, but the more correct view (al-asahh) is to take to protect the dignity of the judiciary and ensure continuity for future needy judges.
The term 'rizq' implies sufficiency (kifayah), not excess.
5
Note the scope of the ruling
The salary is only for sufficiency, and the method is that the ruler appoints the judge without prior condition and then gives a stipend. The passage also touches on timing of payment (beginning of year, aligned with kharaj).
The text is incomplete at the end, mentioning dismissal after taking a year's salary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا باس برزق القاضى لانه عليه السلام بعث عتاب بن اسيد الى مكة وفرض له وبعث عليا الى اليمن وفرض له ولا نه محبوس لحق المسلمين فتكون نفقته فى مالهم وهو مال بيت المال وهذا لان الحبس من اسباب النفقة كما فى الوصى والمضارب اذا سافر بمال المضاربة وهذا فيمايكون كفاية فان كان شرطا فهو حرام لانه استیجار على الطاعة اذا القضاء طاعة بل هو افضلها ترجمہ امام محمد نے فرمایا اور قاضی کے رزق میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے عتاب بن اسید رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کو مکہ کی طرف بھیجا اور ان کیلئے نفقہ مقررفرمایا اور حضرت علی کو یمن کی جانب بھیجا اور ان کیلئے نفقہ مقرر فرمایا اور اسلئے کہ قاضی حق مسلمین میں محبوس ہے تو ہوگا اس کا نفقہ مسلمانوں کے مال میں۔ اور وہ بیت المال کا مال ہے اور یہ اسلئے کہ جس نفقہ کے اسباب میں سے ہے۔ جیسا کہ وصی اور مضارب میں جبکہ مضارب مال مضاربت کے ساتھ سفر کر ہے اور یہ جواز اس مقدار میں ہے جو بقدر کفایت ہو۔ پس اگر شرط ہو تو یہ حرام ہے اسلئے کہ طاعت پر اجرت لینا ہے اسلئے کہ قضاء طاعت بلکہ افضل طاعت ہے۔ تشریح امیر المومنین قاضی کا رزق بیت المال سے دے اور قاضی کے لینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کیونکہ خود آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے عتاب بن اسید کو مکہ کا اور حضرت علی گویمن کا عامل مقر فرمایا اور ان کیلئے نفقہ مقرر فرمایا اور اس زمانہ میں بیت المال نہیں تھا تو آنحضرت اپنے مال سے دیا کرتے تھے (وفیہ تفصیل)
اور چونکہ قاضی مسلمانوں کے امور کیلئے محبوس ہے تو ان کا نفقہ بھی مسلمانوں کے مال میں سے ملنا چاہئے اور مسلمانوں کا مال بیت المال کا مال ہے کیونکہ کسی کیلئے محبوس ہونا اسباب نفقہ میں سے ہے جیسے وصی جبکہ وہ یتیم کے کام میں پھنسا ر ہے تو اس کے مال میں سے اپنا نفقه بقدر کفایت لینا جائز ہے اور ایسے ہی مضارب جبکہ وہ مال مضاربت کو لے کر سفر کرے اسی میں سے بقدر کفایت اپنا نفقہ لے سکتا ہے۔

۳۹۹
كتاب الكراهية
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ لیکن اس کا طریقہ یہ ہوگا کہ امیر قاضی کو مقرر کرے بغیر کسی شرط کے۔ پھر بقدر کفایت اس کو وظیفہ دیا کرے اور اگر پہلے یہ شرط کر لی جائے کہ ماہانہ اتنے روپے لوں گا تو یہ حرام ہے کیونکہ طاعت پر اجرت ہے جو حرام ہے، بلکہ قضاء افضل عبادات میں سے ہے۔ تنبیہ - اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حنفیہ کے نزدیک طاعات پر اجرت لینا حرام ہے اور متاخرین نے بر بناء ضرورت جن طاعات میں اجرت کو جائز قرار دیا ہے وہ وہ طاعات ہیں جس میں ضرورت ہے جیسے تعلیم قرآن اور تعلیم فقہ اور اذان اور امامت۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب محمد یوسف غفر له تاولوی۔
ثم القاضي اذا كان فقيراً فالافضل بل الواجب الاخذ لانه لا يمكنه اقامة فرض القضاء الابه اذا الاشتغال بالكسب يقعده عن اقامته
ترجمہ پھر قاضی اگر فقیر ہو تو افضل بلکہ واجب لینا ہے اس لئے کہ اس کو فرض قضاء کو انجام دیناممکن نہ ہو گا مگر اسی کے ساتھ اور اس لئے کہ کمائی میں مشغول ہونا اس کو فرض کے قائم کرنے سے عاجز کر دے گا۔ تشریح اگر قاضی نادار ہو تو اسکے لئے واجب ہے کہ وہ بیت المال سے رزق لے کیونکہ بغیر رزق کے کام چلے گا نہیں اور اگر کمائی کے اسباب
سلمانوں کا نقصان ہے۔ حضرات حسین نے بیت المال سے بقدر کفایت وظیفہ لیا ہے۔ است اما سے بقدر مالدار قاضی کیلئے بیت المال کے مال سے بچنا افصل ہے
وان كان غنيا فالافضل الامتناع على ما قيل رفقا ببيت المال وقيل الاخذ وهو الاصح صيانة للقضاء عن الهوان ونظرا لمن يولى بعده من المحتاجين لانه اذا انقطع زمانا يتعذر اعادته ثم تسميته رزقا تدل على انه بقدر الكفاية ترجمہ اور اگر قاضی مال دار ہو تو افضل بچنا ہے جیسا کہ کہا گیا ہے بیت المال کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ لینا افضل ہے اور یہی اصح ہے۔ قضاء کو ذلت سے بچانے کیلئے اور اس شخص پر شفقت کرتے ہوئے جو اس کے بعد محتاجوں میں سے قاضی بنایا جائے اس لئے کہ رزق جبکہ ایک زمانہ تک منقطع رہا تو اس کا اعادہ مستعد رہو گا۔ پھر اس کا نام رزق رکھنا اس بات پر دلالت کرتا ہے کہ یہ بقدر کفایت ہے۔ تشریح اور اگر قاضی تو نگر ہے تو اس میں دو قول ہیں۔ دو ہے۔
- بیت المال سے رزق نہ لینا افضل ہے تا کہ بیت المال کی رعایت ہو سکے۔ -۲- لینا افضل ہے اور یہی اصح ہے کیونکہ جب سرکاری تمام کاموں میں بہت سے پیسے خرچ کئے بہاتے ہیں اور عہدہ قضاء کو قاضی اور دوسری وجہ یہ بھی ہے کہ جب اسکے بعد دوسرا قاضی مقرر ہوگا جونا دار ہوتو اسکو پریشانی مفت انجام دے تو لوگ اس منصب کو ذلیل سمجھیں گے۔ حالانکہ یہ سب سے اونچا کام یہ کی نظمی سے اسکا وظیفہ جاری ہونے میں تاخیر ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ایسے موقع پر نیا اندراج فورا نہیں ہو پاتا۔ پھر اس کو رزق کہا گیا ہے یہ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ یہ وظیفہ بقدر کفایت ملے گا۔
وقد جرى الرسم باعطائه فى اول السنة لان الخراج يوخذ في اول السنة وهو يعطى منه وفي زماننا الخراج يوخذ فى اخر السنة والماخوذ من الخراج خراج السنة الماضية هو الصحيح ولو استوفى رزق سنة وعزل
He (Imam Muhammad) said: There is no harm in the salary of the judge, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) sent 'Attab ibn Asid to Mecca and fixed a stipend for him, and sent 'Ali to Yemen and fixed a stipend for him, and because the judge is occupied for the rights of Muslims, so his expenditure is in their wealth, which is the wealth of Bayt al-Mal. This is because being occupied is among the causes of expenditure, as with the executor and the mudarib when he travels with mudarabah wealth. This is in what is sufficient. If it is conditional, then it is haram, because it is hiring for obedience, since judgment is obedience, rather it is the best of obedience. Translation: Imam Muhammad said: There is no harm in the judge's salary. Because the Prophet sent 'Attab ibn Asid to Mecca and fixed a stipend for him, and sent 'Ali to Yemen and fixed a stipend for him, and because the judge is occupied for the rights of Muslims, so his expenditure is from their wealth, which is the wealth of Bayt al-Mal. This is because being occupied is among the causes of expenditure, as with the executor and the mudarib when he travels with mudarabah wealth. This permissibility is to the extent of sufficiency. If it is conditional, then it is haram, because it is hiring for obedience, since judgment is obedience, rather it is the best of obedience. The commentary: The Amir al-Mu'minin should give the judge his salary from Bayt al-Mal, and there is no harm in the judge taking it, because the Prophet himself appointed 'Attab to Mecca and 'Ali to Yemen and fixed stipends for them, and at that time there was no Bayt al-Mal, so the Prophet gave from his own wealth. And since the judge is occupied for the affairs of the Muslims, his expenditure should come from the Muslims' wealth, which is Bayt al-Mal. Being occupied for someone is among the causes of expenditure, like the executor when he is engaged in the orphan's affairs, he may take his own sufficiency from the orphan's wealth, and similarly the mudarib when he travels with mudarabah wealth, he may take his sufficiency from it. Page 400: ... But the method is that the Amir appoints the judge without any condition. Then he gives him a stipend to the extent of sufficiency. If a condition is made beforehand that he will take so many rupees monthly, then it is haram, because it is payment for obedience, which is haram, especially since judgment is among the best acts of worship. A note: From this it is known that, according to the Hanafis, taking payment for acts of worship is haram. The later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) have allowed payment for certain acts of worship out of necessity, such as teaching the Quran, teaching fiqh, the adhan, and imamah. And Allah knows best. Then, if the judge is poor, the preferable, rather obligatory, is to take, because he cannot establish the duty of judgment except by it, since engaging in earning would incapacitate him from establishing it. Translation: Then if the judge is poor, the preferable, rather obligatory, is to take, because he cannot perform the duty of judgment except through it, and because engaging in earning would incapacitate him from establishing it. Commentary: If the judge is needy, it is obligatory for him to take salary from Bayt al-Mal, because without salary the work cannot proceed, and if he engages in earning, it would harm the Muslims... And if he is wealthy, the preferable is to abstain, as has been said, out of consideration for Bayt al-Mal, and it has been said that taking is preferable, and this is the more correct (asahh), to protect the judiciary from contempt, and out of consideration for the needy person who will be appointed after him, because if the salary is discontinued for a time, its restoration becomes difficult. Then, naming it 'salary' indicates that it is to the extent of sufficiency. Commentary: If the judge is wealthy, there are two views: (1) Not taking from Bayt al-Mal is preferable to preserve Bayt al-Mal. (2) Taking is preferable, and this is more correct, because if he foregoes it, future needy judges may not get it, and the office may be looked down upon. Then, the term 'salary' indicates that it is sufficient. And custom has prevailed that it is given at the beginning of the year, because kharaj is taken at the beginning of the year and it is given from it. In our time, kharaj is taken at the end of the year, and the correct view is that what is taken from kharaj is the kharaj of the past year. If he takes his salary for a year and then is dismissed...
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of a judge's salary (rizq al-qadi) from the public treasury (Bayt al-Mal). The central ruling is that there is no harm in a judge receiving a stipend, provided it is given without prior condition. The proof is based on the Prophet's practice of appointing governors and providing them stipends. The legal reasoning is that the judge is occupied for the benefit of Muslims, akin to an executor (wasi) or a mudarib, who may take their expenses from the trust property. However, if the salary is stipulated as a condition of appointment, it becomes haram because it amounts to hiring for an act of worship ('ibadah). The passage then distinguishes between a poor judge and a wealthy judge: for the poor judge, it is obligatory (wajib) to accept the salary to fulfill the duty of judgment; for the wealthy judge, the more correct view is that taking the salary is preferable to maintain the dignity of the office and ensure continuity for future needy judges. The passage also discusses the timing: customarily, salary is given at the beginning of the year, aligned with kharaj collection. The term 'rizq' (salary) implies sufficiency (kifayah), not excess.

Key Terms
رزق القاضي (rizq al-qadi): The salary or stipend given to a judge from the public treasury for his services.
بيت المال (bayt al-mal): The public treasury of the Islamic state, used for the welfare of Muslims.
كفاية (kifayah): Sufficiency; the salary should be enough for basic needs, not excessive.
محبوس (mahbus): Occupied, confined; the judge is 'occupied' for the sake of Muslims' rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when is a judge's salary considered haram?
A) When the judge is wealthy and takes it voluntarily.
B) When the salary is stipulated as a condition of the appointment.
C) When the judge is poor and does not take it.
D) When the salary exceeds the amount of sufficiency.

Key Takeaway
A judge's salary from Bayt al-Mal is permissible without condition, but becomes haram if stipulated; for a poor judge it is obligatory, and for a wealthy judge the more correct view is to take it to maintain the dignity of the judiciary.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on a Judge Taking Salary from Bayt al-Mal
Ruling on judge's salary with conditions and exceptions for wages for worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge's salary, distinguish between the obligations of a poor versus wealthy judge, and identify the condition that makes a salary forbidden.

Core Idea
A poor judge must take a salary; a wealthy judge should take it to protect the judiciary's dignity — but upfront conditions make it forbidden.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah examines the delicate balance between the prohibition of wages for worship and the necessity of supporting judges. It clarifies that judgeship is an act of worship, yet the public interest requires that judges be sustained. The text provides a nuanced ruling based on the judge's financial status and the manner of appointment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Taking salary for serving as a judge. What is the legal classification? It depends on whether a condition was stipulated beforehand and on the judge's wealth.
The act is not inherently prohibited; the prohibition arises from stipulating wages for worship.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios: poor vs. wealthy judge
For a poor judge, taking salary is obligatory (wājib) because he cannot perform his duty otherwise. For a wealthy judge, there are two views: abstaining is better (to protect Bayt al-Māl) or taking is better (to protect the dignity of the office). The text says the latter is correct (aṣaḥḥ).
The terminology 'rizq' indicates sustenance according to sufficiency, not contractual wages.
3
Analyze the condition of prior stipulation
If a judge makes it a condition before appointment that he will receive a fixed monthly salary, that is forbidden (haram) because it is wages for an act of worship. If the ruler gives an unconditional stipend after appointment, it is permissible.
This distinction is critical: the prohibition is on the condition, not the taking per se.
4
Explore the underlying principle: wages for worship
Judgeship is among the best acts of worship; taking wages for worship is generally forbidden. Later scholars permitted wages for necessary acts like teaching Quran, fiqh, adhan, and imamah due to necessity.
This is a concession (rukhsah) not the original rule.
5
Note the preferred view within the Hanafi school
For the wealthy judge, the preferred view (muftā bihi) is that taking is better, to preserve the judiciary's honor and to ensure future needy judges receive salaries.
The text weighs public interest (maslahah) over immediate treasury benefit.

اورنت
وقد جرى الرسم باعطائه فى اول السنة لان الخراج يوخذ في اول السنة وهو يعطى منه وفي زماننا الخراج يوخذ فى اخر السنة والماخوذ من الخراج خراج السنة الماضية هو الصحيح ولو استوفى رزق سنة وعزل
قبل استكمالها قيل هو على اختلاف معروف فى نفقة المرأة اذا ماتت في السنة بعد استعجال نفقة السنة الاصح انه يجب الرد
ترجمہ اور رسم جاری ہے رزق کو دینے کی سال کے شروع میں اسلئے کہ خراج لیا جاتا تھا سال کے شروع میں اور رزق دیا جاتا ہے اس سے ( خراج سے ) اور ہمارے زمانے میں خراج لیا جاتا ہے سال کے آخر میں اور جو خراج کیا جاتا ہے وہ سال گذشتہ کا خراج ہوتا ہے۔ یہی صحیح ہے اور اگر قاضی نے سال بھر کا رزق وصول کر لیا اور سال کے مکمل ہونے سے پہلے مر گیا۔ کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ اس اختلاف پر ہے جو پہچان لیا گیا ہے بیوی کے نفقہ کے بارے میں جبکہ وہ مر جائے سال کے درمیان میں سال کا نفقہ متجمل لینے کے بعد اور اصبح یہ ہے
کہ واپس واجب ہے۔
تشریح مصنف فرماتے ہیں رزق وغیرہ خراج میں سے دیا جاتا ہے۔ اور متقدمین کے زمانہ میں خراج لینے کی عادت سال کے شروع میں تھی تو رزق بھی سال کے شروع میں دیا جاتا تھا لیکن ہمارے زمانہ میں خراج سال کے آخر میں لیا جاتا ہے تو رزق بھی سال کے آخر میں دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر قاضی نے سال کے شروع میں سال بھر کا نفقہ وصول کر لیا اور سال کے مکمل ہونے سے پہلے ہی مر گیا تو فرماتے ہیں کہ اصح قول کے مطابق اس کی واپسی کرنی ہوگی۔
Book of Disliked Matters. Ashraf al-Bidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Vol. 13. But its method is that the ruler appoints a judge without any condition. Then he gives him a stipend according to sufficiency. And if beforehand he makes the condition that 'I will take so many rupees monthly,' then it is forbidden because it is payment for an act of worship, which is forbidden. Indeed, judgeship is among the best acts of worship. Note: From this it is understood that in the Hanafi school, taking wages for acts of worship is forbidden. And the later scholars, due to necessity, declared permissible wages for those acts of worship that have necessity, such as teaching the Qur'an, teaching fiqh, adhan, and imamah. And Allah knows best. Muhammad Yusuf, may he be forgiven, from Tolawi. 20. Now tricks for wages for recitation of the Qur'an are also sought, and common huffaz take wages for reciting the Qur'an. This is absolutely forbidden. Contemplate. Muhammad Yusuf, may he be forgiven. For a poor judge, taking from Bayt al-Mal is obligatory. Then, if the judge is poor, the preferred (view) is, rather it is obligatory, to take, because he cannot perform the obligatory duty of judgeship except with it, and because engaging in earning would incapacitate him from performing it. Translation: Then if the judge is poor, it is preferable, rather obligatory, to take, because it will not be possible for him to perform the obligatory duty of judgeship except with this, and because being occupied with earning will incapacitate him from establishing the obligation. Explanation: If the judge is poor, it is obligatory for him to take sustenance from the Bayt al-Mal, because without sustenance the work will not proceed, and if he has means of earning... the Muslims' loss. Imam Husayn took a stipend from Bayt al-Mal according to sufficiency. And from there, against possibility: for a wealthy judge, it is better to avoid the wealth of Bayt al-Mal. And if he is rich, then it is better to abstain, as has been said, out of consideration for Bayt al-Mal; and it has been said that taking is better, and this is the correct (view), to protect the judiciary from contempt, and out of consideration for whoever after him from the needy, because if it is cut off for a time, its revival becomes difficult. Then naming it 'sustenance' indicates that it is according to sufficiency. Translation: And if the judge is wealthy, then it is better to abstain, as has been said, out of consideration for Bayt al-Mal; and it has been said that taking is better, and this is the correct (view). To protect the judiciary from humiliation, and out of kindness to the person who after him will be appointed judge from among the needy, because if the sustenance is cut off for a time, its revival will be difficult. Then calling it 'sustenance' indicates that it is according to sufficiency. Explanation: And if the judge is wealthy, then there are two sayings. Two: 1) Not taking sustenance from Bayt al-Mal is better, so that Bayt al-Mal may be preserved. 2) Taking is better, and this is correct, because when in all government affairs a lot of money is spent, and the office of judgeship... and the second reason is also that when after him another judge will be appointed who is needy, then if he is given this with difficulty, people will consider this position lowly. Although it is the highest work, due to the system, there will be a delay in the issuance of his stipend. Because at such an occasion, a new registration cannot happen immediately. Then it is called 'sustenance' – this is evidence that this stipend will be given according to sufficiency. From which account of Bayt al-Mal will salaries be given? And the custom has been to give it at the beginning of the year, because kharaj was taken at the beginning of the year and it is given from it. And in our time, kharaj is taken at the end of the year, and what is taken from kharaj is the kharaj of the past year; this is correct. And if a judge takes sustenance for a year and is dismissed before its completion, it is said that this is on the well-known difference regarding the maintenance of a woman if she dies during the year after taking the maintenance for the year in advance; the correct view is that refund is obligatory. Translation: And the custom is to give sustenance at the beginning of the year, because kharaj used to be taken at the beginning of the year and sustenance is given from it. And in our time, kharaj is taken at the end of the year, and what is taken as kharaj is the kharaj of the past year. This is correct. And if a judge takes sustenance for a whole year and dies before its completion, it is said that this is on the well-known difference regarding the maintenance of a woman when she dies during the year after taking the year's maintenance in advance; the correct view is that refund is obligatory. Explanation: The author says that sustenance etc. is given from kharaj. In the time of the early scholars, the custom was to take kharaj at the beginning of the year, so sustenance was also given at the beginning of the year. But in our time, kharaj is taken at the end of the year, so sustenance will also be given at the end of the year. And if a judge takes the whole year's maintenance at the beginning of the year and dies before the year completes, the author says that according to the correct view, he must return it.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah, discusses the ruling on a judge taking a salary. The passage type is a ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The text opens by stating that a ruler should appoint a judge without any condition of salary beforehand. If a condition is stipulated (e.g., 'I will take so much monthly'), it is forbidden because wages for acts of worship are forbidden. Judgeship is an act of worship. However, later Hanafi scholars (mutā'khkhirūn) permitted wages for certain acts of worship due to necessity, such as teaching the Qur'an, teaching fiqh, adhan, and imamah. The commentator then strongly condemns the practice of taking money for reciting the Qur'an, calling it absolutely forbidden. The main ruling: if a judge is poor (faqīr), it is preferable (afḍal) and even obligatory (wājib) for him to take sustenance from the public treasury (Bayt al-Māl) because otherwise he cannot fulfill his duty. If he is wealthy (ghaniyy), there are two views: the first says it is better to abstain out of consideration for Bayt al-Māl; the second says taking is better and this is the correct view (aṣaḥḥ) to protect the dignity of the judiciary and to ensure that future needy judges can receive payment—if the stipend is stopped, it is difficult to restart. The stipend is called 'rizq' (sustenance), indicating it is given according to sufficiency. The passage also discusses timing: traditionally kharāj (land tax) was collected at the beginning of the year, so salaries were given then; but in the author's time, kharāj was collected at the end, so salaries should be given at the end. If a judge takes a year's salary in advance and dies before the year ends, the correct view is that refund is obligatory, analogous to the case of a wife who takes maintenance in advance and dies mid-year.

Key Terms
قاض (qāḍī): A judge appointed by the ruler to adjudicate disputes according to Islamic law.
بیت المال (bayt al-māl): The public treasury of the Muslim state, from which salaries for judges and other officials are paid.
رزق (rizq): Sustenance or stipend given from the public treasury to a judge, meant to cover his needs (bi qadr al-kifāyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling for a poor judge regarding taking sustenance from Bayt al-Mal?
A) It is haram because judgeship is an act of worship.
B) It is preferable and obligatory (afḍal bal wājib) for him to take.
C) It is better for him to abstain to preserve the treasury.
D) He should make a condition for a fixed salary before appointment.

Key Takeaway
A judge's salary from Bayt al-Mal is permissible only if given unconditionally; poor judges must take it, while wealthy judges are encouraged to take it to uphold the judiciary's honor.
